The Saved Status of Ahl al-Fatra and the Three Opinions
Sanusi states the saved status of Ahl al-Fatra and enumerates three scholarly opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic doctrine regarding the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah), including the saved status of the Prophet's ancestors, and the three scholarly opinions on their fate.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Fatra are saved; the Prophet's ancestors are in Paradise.

This passage from Sanusi clarifies a crucial aspect of Islamic theology: the fate of those who never received a prophetic message. After presenting the correct view that they are saved, Sanusi addresses misunderstandings about the Prophet's lineage and then enumerates three opinions on the matter. Pay close attention to how he uses Qur'anic and hadith evidence to support his position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the key terms and the flow from general principle to specific cases.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the sentence that states the correct doctrine (al-madhhab al-ḥaqq) and note its key components: that Ahl al-Fatra are saved, including the Prophet's ancestors.
3
Examine the evidence
Observe the two proofs cited: the Qur'anic verse (26:219) and the hadith about the Prophet's transfer. Understand why they support the saved status.
4
Follow the correction of errors
See how Sanusi refutes the claims about Āzar and Abū Ḥanīfah, and the interpretation of the prohibition to seek forgiveness.
5
Analyze the three opinions
List the three opinions and understand which is correct and why.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المذهب الحق أن أهل الفترة على التحقيق ناجون، وأن منهم آباءه وكذا أمهاته ، من عبد الله إلى آدم ممن لم تبلغهم دعوة نبي ولا رسول، فكلهم ناجون وفي الجنة، ومحكوم بإيمانهم ولم يدخلهم كفر ولا رجس ولا عيب، ولا شيء مما كان عليه الجاهلية بأدلة نقلية منها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتَقَلُّبَكَ فِي السَّاجِدِينَ ﴾ [الشعراء: ۲۱۹] ومنها قوله : «لم أزل أنتقل من الأصلاب الطاهرات إلى الأرحام الزاكيات إلى آخر الأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر والقطع ، وأما آزر فكان عم إبراهيم، وإنما دعاه بالأب على عادة العرب ولا يعول على غيرها ولا يلتفت إليه أصلا لضعفه أو نسخه ، هذا هو الحق الذي نلقى الله به. وأما ما نقل عن أبي حنفية في الفقه الأكبر من أن والدي المصطفى كانا كذلك فهو مكذوب عليه ، وحاشاه أن يقول في والدي المصطفى ذلك على الإطلاق، فهو مدسوس عليه بفرض «الفقه الأكبر» له ، وأما على أنه ليس له وإنما نسب إليه فلا يحتاج للجواب عنه، أو يقال إنهما ماتا في زمن الكفر بمعنى الجاهلية وإن كانا ناجيين ، وغلط ملّا علي القاري يغفر له في كلمة شنيعة قالها ، ومن العجائب ما نُسب له مع ذلك من إيمان فرعون، وأما ما ورد من نهي الله عن استغفاره لهما فمحمول على أنه قبل إخباره بحالهما، أو لئلا تقتدي به أولاد الكفار الماضين، والحاصل أن أهل الفترة فيهم ثلاثة أقوال: أولها: وهو الصحيح أنهم لا يعذبون وإن غيروا وبدلوا أو عبدوا الأصنام. ويدخل الجنَّة (1)؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولًا ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٥] . قال الحافظ (۲) في «الإصابة»: وَرَدَ من عِدَّة طُرُق في حقٌّ الشَّيخ الهرم (۳) ، ومَن مات في الفَتْرَة (٤) ، ومَن وُلِد أَكْمَهَ أعمى أصم(٥) ، ومَن وُلِد مجنوناً ، أو = ثانيها: وهو ضعيف أنهم إن لم يغيروا ولم يبدلوا ولم يعبدوا الأصنام فلا يعذبون . وثالثها: وهو أضعف مما قبله أنهم في النار مطلقا. انتهى الشنواني.
Know that the correct doctrine is that the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) are truly saved, and among them are his fathers and likewise his mothers, from ʿAbdullāh to Adam, those whom the call of no prophet or messenger reached. So all of them are saved and in Paradise, and they are judged to have faith; no disbelief, impurity, defect, or anything of the state of ignorance entered them, based on transmitted proofs, including His statement: {And your turning among those who prostrate} [26:219], and including his statement: 'I have not ceased to transfer from pure loins to pure wombs' — to the end of the hadiths that reach the level of tawātur and definitiveness. As for Āzar, he was the uncle of Abraham, and he only called him 'father' according to the custom of the Arabs; no attention is paid to other [interpretations] nor is it considered at all due to its weakness or abrogation. This is the truth with which we meet Allah. As for what is reported from Abū Ḥanīfah in al-Fiqh al-Akbar that the Prophet’s parents were like that, it is falsely attributed to him; far be it from him to say that about the Prophet’s parents absolutely; it is interpolated into his book assuming al-Fiqh al-Akbar is his. As for the view that it is not his and only attributed to him, then no answer is needed. Or it is said that they died in the time of disbelief in the sense of jāhiliyyah while being saved. The error of Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī — may he be forgiven — in an ugly word he said. And among the wonders is what is attributed to him besides that of the faith of Pharaoh. As for the prohibition of Allah to seek forgiveness for them, it is interpreted as being before informing him of their state, or so that the children of past disbelievers would not follow his example. The summary: Regarding the people of the interval, there are three opinions: First, which is correct, that they are not punished even if they changed, altered, or worshipped idols. They enter Paradise; due to His statement: {And We were not punishers until We send a messenger} [17:15]. Al-Ḥāfiẓ said in al-Iṣābah: It has been reported through multiple chains concerning the decrepit old man, and those who died in the interval, and those born blind, blind and deaf, and those born insane, or... Second, which is weak, that if they did not change, alter, or worship idols, then they are not punished. Third, which is weaker than the previous, that they are in the Fire absolutely. End of al-Shanwānī.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the correct doctrine (madhhab ḥaqq) regarding the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) — those who lived in periods between prophets. The author affirms that they are saved and enter Paradise, based on textual evidence from the Qur’an and hadith. He clarifies that the Prophet’s ancestors are included, and addresses the issue of Āzar (Abraham’s uncle). He also refutes the alleged statement of Abū Ḥanīfah about the Prophet’s parents, considering it a forgery. Then he summarizes three scholarly opinions on Ahl al-Fitra: (1) the correct view: they are not punished even if they changed religion; (2) a weak view: they are only not punished if they did not change; (3) a weaker view: they are in Hell absolutely. The passage ends with a citation from al-Ḥāfiẓ Ibn Ḥajar listing categories of people included in this ruling.

Key Terms
أهل الفترة
ناجون
آزر
الفقه الأكبر
مكذوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ahl al-Fatra are automatically punished for not believing.
Correction: The correct view is that they are saved due to lack of revelation, as supported by the verse 'We were not punishers until We send a messenger'.

Checkpoint
According to the correct view, what happens to someone born blind who never received any prophetic call?
A) They are punished for not believing.
B) They are saved and enter Paradise.
C) They are in a state of limbo.
D) They are resurrected as animals.

Key Takeaway
The correct view is that all people of the interval are saved and in Paradise, based on the Qur'an and hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah does not punish those who never received a messenger, how does this affect your view of people of other faiths or none? Do you feel compelled to share the message knowing its necessity?
?
The Prophet's ancestors were saved by Allah's mercy despite living in jahiliyyah. Are you relying on your own deeds for salvation or on Allah's mercy? What would change if you truly internalized that?
?
The correct opinion states even idol worshippers among Ahl al-Fatra are saved. Does this stretch your understanding of accountability? How can you still take your own faith seriously without presuming on Allah's mercy?

The Six Categories Exempt from Punishment
Shanwani defines the six types of people not punished due to lack of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six categories of people who are not punished due to lack of revelation and the rationale behind their exemption.

Core Idea
Six groups are excused from punishment because they never received a clear divine message.

This lesson explains a key exception to the general rule of accountability. The hadith identifies six types of individuals who, due to physical or mental conditions or living in a period without prophets, are not held accountable. Al-Shanwānī's commentary clarifies each category and resolves a common misconception about the term 'akmah'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once, then read its English translation. Pay attention to the sequence of categories and the commentator's clarifications.
The passage begins by explaining that entering Paradise is by grace, not reward, which sets the context.
2
Identify the six categories
Look for the list of six categories: decrepit old man (shaykh haram), one who died in the interval (fatrah), one born imbecile (akmah), blind and deaf, born insane, and one who becomes insane before maturity.
Note that 'akmah' is glossed as 'mentally deficient' rather than physically blind.
3
Understand the linguistic clarifications
Observe how the commentator distinguishes between fatrah (interval), fitrah (nature), and faqrah (verse segment). This shows careful attention to terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويدخل الجنة أي بمخض فضل الله تعالى فليس ثوابا إذ لا عمل فلا ينافي تقدير وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ﴾ [الإسراء: (١٥] أي: ولا مثيبين الأمير. (۳) قوله: (الشيخ الهرم أي : الذي بلغ به الهرم إلى اختلال عقله، ولم تبلغه الدعوة قبل ذلك ، بدليل قوله بَعْدُ : (لو عقلت) ، وإلا فهو إذا كان شيخا هرما عاقلا بلغته الدعوة فهو كغيره من المكلفين . الشنواني . (٤) قوله: (ومن مات في الفترة هم الأمم الكائنون بين أزمنة الرسل، ولم يرسل إليهم الأول ولا أدركم الثاني، فيشمل ما بين محمد وعيسى ، ويشمل العرب الذين بين إسماعيل ونبينا ، والفترة من الفتور ، وهو الغفلة والترك ; لأنهم تركوا بلا رسول ، وأما الخلقة فيقال لها الفطرة ، وأما الفقرة فهي في السجع كشطر البيت في النظم الشنواني . (٥) قوله: (أعمى) كان الأولى أن يقول : ومن ولد أكمه أو أعمى أو أصم، فإن الأكمه وحده كان بالمعنى الآتي له ، فالمراد به الأبله الذي لا تمييز عنده، وليس المراد به وليس المراد به من طمست عيناه ، فالشيخ الهرم قسم أول ، ومن مات في الفترة قسم ثاني ، ومن ولد أكمه قسم ثالث ، والأعمى والأصم قسم رابع ، ومن ولد مجنونا قسم خامس ، ومن طرأ عليه قبل أن يبلغ قسم سادس. الشنواني .
His saying: 'And they enter Paradise' means by sheer grace of Allah Almighty, so it is not a reward since there is no deed, so it does not contradict the estimation of {And We were not punishers} [17:15], meaning nor bestowers of reward. (3) His saying: 'the decrepit old man' refers to one who has reached decrepitude to the point of mental derangement, and the call did not reach him before that, as evidenced by his subsequent saying 'if you had reason'; otherwise, if he is a decrepit old man who is rational and the call reached him, then he is like other responsible persons. (4) His saying: 'those who died in the interval' are the nations that existed between the times of messengers; the first did not reach them nor did the second overtake them. This includes what is between Muhammad and Jesus, and includes the Arabs between Ishmael and our Prophet. The interval (al-fatrah) is from al-fatūr, which is heedlessness and abandonment, because they were left without a messenger. As for al-khilqah (creation), it is called al-fiṭrah; as for al-faqrah (verse/prose segment), it is in rhyme like a hemistich in poetry. (5) His saying: 'blind' — it would have been better for him to say: 'and those born blind (akmah) or blind or deaf', for akmah by itself has the meaning that follows. What is meant is the imbecile who has no discernment, not the one whose eyes are sealed. So the decrepit old man is the first category; those who died in the interval are the second category; those born imbecile are the third category; the blind and deaf are the fourth category; those born insane are the fifth category; those who became insane before reaching maturity are the sixth category.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Shanwānī on the report of al-Ḥāfiẓ Ibn Ḥajar. It first explains that entering Paradise is by grace, not reward, so it does not contradict the verse about punishment. Then it defines three categories: (1) the decrepit old man whose mind has failed and the message never reached him; (2) those who died in the interval between prophets; (3) those born blind (akmah), which means mentally deficient, not physically blind. The passage then lists six categories in total: (1) decrepit old man, (2) one who died in the interval, (3) one born imbecile (akmah), (4) blind and deaf, (5) born insane, (6) one who becomes insane before maturity. The commentator clarifies linguistic nuances, distinguishing fatrah (interval) from fiṭrah (nature) and faqrah (verse segment).

Key Terms
الشيخ الهرم
الفترة
أكمه
أعمى
أصم
مجنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'akmah' in this hadith refers to someone who is physically blind.
Correction: Al-Shanwānī explicitly states that 'akmah' means mentally deficient (ablah) with no discernment, not one whose eyes are sealed.

Checkpoint
How many categories of people are excused according to the hadith?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The hadith identifies six types of people who are not punished due to lack of revelation: the decrepit old man, those who died in the interval, the mentally deficient, the blind and deaf, the born insane, and those who become insane before maturity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have received clear revelation through the Qur'an and Sunnah. Are you truly grateful for this gift, or do you take it for granted while others never had the chance to hear it? What will you do today to live in gratitude?
?
The hadith exempts those who never received the message. But you have received it. Will you stand before Allah without excuse on the Day of Judgment? What are you doing right now to ensure you act upon what you know?
?
If you were among those born with sound intellect and access to revelation, you have no excuse. Does this thought burden you? What is one specific area of your obedience where you have been negligent, and when will you correct it?

The Test for Those Who Never Received the Message
Ibn Hajar narrates a hadith about the test for those who never received the message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of people who are tested on the Day of Judgment according to the hadith narrated by Ibn Hajar, and the nature of the divine test for those who never received the prophetic message.

Core Idea
God's justice tests those who never heard the message in an intelligible form.

This lesson examines a hadith narrated by Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani that describes how Allah will test a specific group of people on the Day of Judgment. These are individuals who never received the prophetic message in a clear form due to various circumstances. The narration lists several categories and outlines the procedure of their test. Understanding this hadith helps us appreciate the comprehensiveness of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the categories mentioned.
Focus on the list of people described.
2
Identify the categories
List the five types of people mentioned: the elderly senile, one who died in the fatrah, one born blind/deaf (akmah), one born insane, and one who became insane before puberty.
The hadith uses the term 'akmah' which means blind and deaf.
3
Understand the test
Notice that they will be shown a fire and told to enter it. They respond by saying they understood or were reminded and believed.
4
Reflect on theological implications
This shows that God's judgment takes into account individual circumstances. Those who never heard the message are not simply condemned or saved without examination.
The test demonstrates divine justice.
5
Address common misconceptions
This test does not guarantee that all ahl al-fatrah will pass and be saved. It is a trial, and the outcome depends on their response.
The hadith only describes the test, not the final result.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ في «الإصابة»: وَرَدَ من عِدَّة طُرُق في حقِّ الشَّيخ الهرم، ومَن مات في الفَتْرَة، ومَن وُلِد أَكْمَهَ أعمى أصم، ومَن وُلِد مجنوناً، أو طرأ عليه الجنون قبل أن يبلغ ونحو ذلك، أنَّ كلَّا منهم يُدلي بحجةٍ ويقول: عَقَلْتُ أو ذُكِّرْتُ آمَنْتُ، فترفع لهم نارٌ، ويقال لهم: ادخلوها
Al-Hafiz said in al-Isabah: It is reported from multiple chains concerning the elderly senile, and one who died in the period (fatrah), and one who was born blind (akmah) blind and deaf, and one who was born insane, or one to whom insanity occurred before reaching puberty and similar cases, that each of them will present a proof and say: 'I understood or I was reminded and I believed.' So a fire will be raised for them, and they will be told: 'Enter it.'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration cited by Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in his work al-Isabah. It lists the categories of people who did not receive the prophetic message in this world: the elderly who have lost their mental faculties to senility, those who lived in a period between prophets (fatrah), those born blind or deaf or both, those born insane, and those who became insane before reaching puberty. These individuals will be tested on the Day of Judgment: they will be shown a fire and commanded to enter it. Their response will be based on whether they recognize the truth. The narration thus establishes a principle for the divine justice regarding those who never heard the message in an intelligible form.

Key Terms
الشيخ الهرم
الفترة
الأكمه
الجنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith guarantees that all ahl al-fatrah will enter Paradise because they will pass the test.
Correction: The hadith only describes the test itself, not the outcome. It does not say all will enter the fire or be saved; it only states they will be tested. The test is a demonstration of divine justice, and the result depends on their response.

Checkpoint
How many categories of people are explicitly mentioned in the hadith as being tested on the Day of Judgment?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
God tests those who never received the prophetic message in a clear form by presenting them with a fire; their response demonstrates their innate recognition of truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had been born in a time or place with no clear message from God, would your innate sense of truth have been enough to recognize Him? What does your answer say about the state of your heart right now?
?
The hadith mentions the test of the fire. When you face a difficult trial in your life, do you respond with the same submission that the truthful believers will show? Are you truly prepared to obey God even when it costs you everything?
?
You have received the message clearly. How will you answer when you stand before God and He asks you why you did not live by it? What proof will you offer?

Ahl al-Fatrah: The Correct Ruling of Salvation
Al-Amir concludes that ahl al-fatrah are saved, refuting contrary views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic ruling on the people of the fatrah and the rationale behind their salvation, including the distinction between obligation and compulsion in the Hereafter.

Core Idea
All ahl al-fatrah are saved by divine mercy, regardless of their actions.

Al-Amir addresses a delicate theological question: what happens to people who never received a prophetic message? He navigates between conflicting reports and established principles to affirm that they are saved. This lesson unpacks his argument, distinguishing between obligation and compulsion in the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term ahl al-fatrah
Learn who the ahl al-fatrah are—people who lived in periods without a prophet—and why their fate is debated.
2
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then follow with the translation to grasp al-Amir's flow.
Notice the technical terms: taklif, qahr wa jabr.
3
Grasp the key distinction
Focus on why the command to enter the fire is not a binding obligation (taklif) but an act of compulsion (qahr wa jabr). This is central to the argument.
Obligation only applies in this world; the Hereafter is for recompense.
4
Examine the handling of conflicting reports
See how al-Amir deals with reports that some ahl al-fatrah might be punished—he categorizes them as weak (ahad) or exceptional.
This shows the principle that certain (qat'i) evidence takes precedence.
5
Reflect on the conclusion and its implications
Understand that the truth (al-haqq) is that all ahl al-fatrah are saved, and imagine how this reflects on divine mercy and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الأمير: قوله : فترفع لهم نار ... الخ) أي جهنم أو غيرها، ويحتمل خلود الآبين فيها وعدمه، ويحتاج لتصحيح نقل صريح ، ثم هذا ليس أمر تكليف بدخولها إذ لا تكليف في الآخرة ، وإنما هو قهر وجبر كما في حاشية الملوي، أي لأن المولى في ذلك اليوم كما هذا الصحيح يغضب غضبا ما غضب مثله قط فلا يُسئل عما يفعل ، وبعد فكلام ابن حجر مقابل للأصح كما في حاشية شيخنا ، والحق أن أهل الفترة ناجون، وأطلق الأئمة: ولو بدلوا وغيَّروا وعبدوا الأصنام، كما في حاشية الملوي، وما ورد في بعضهم من العذاب ؛ إما أنه آحادٌ لا يُعارِض القطع ، أو أنه لمعنى يخُصُّ ذلك البعض يعلمه الله تعالى .
Al-Amir said: His statement: 'a fire will be raised for them... etc.' i.e., Hellfire or other, and it is possible that the disobedient will abide therein or not, and this requires a clear transmission for verification. Then this is not a command of obligation to enter it, for there is no obligation in the Hereafter; rather it is coercion and compulsion, as in the marginal gloss of al-Malawi. That is because the Master on that day, as this correct report states, becomes angry with a anger the like of which has never been, so He is not asked about what He does. After this, the statement of Ibn Hajar is opposite to the more correct view, as in the marginal gloss of our teacher. The truth is that the people of the fatrah are saved, and the imams have stated unequivocally: even if they changed, altered, and worshipped idols, as in the marginal gloss of al-Malawi. And whatever has come regarding punishment for some of them is either that it is solitary reports (ahad) that do not contradict the certain, or it is due to a meaning specific to that individual, which Allah knows.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument by al-Amir concerning the fate of ahl al-fatrah (people who never received a prophetic message). He first comments on the hadith of the fire test, clarifying that the fire could be Hell or something else, and the duration of punishment (for those who fail) is uncertain. He emphasizes that the command to enter the fire is not a binding obligation (taklif) because there is no obligation in the Hereafter; it is an act of divine compulsion (qahr wa jabr). He cites al-Malawi's gloss to explain that Allah's anger on that day is unprecedented and He is not questioned about His actions. Al-Amir then states that Ibn Hajar's interpretation (possibly implying that some ahl al-fatrah may be punished) is contrary to the more correct view (al-asahh). The truth (al-haqq) is that all ahl al-fatrah are saved (najun), and the imams have even said this applies if they had changed and worshipped idols. Any reports of punishment for some are either weak solitary hadiths that cannot override certain knowledge, or refer to special cases known only to Allah.

Key Terms
أهل الفترة
الآخرة
تكليف
قهر وجبر
الآحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-fatrah are held accountable and some will be punished.
Correction: They are all saved even if they worshipped idols, because they never received a clear message and there is no obligation in the Hereafter.

Checkpoint
According to al-Amir, what is the ruling on ahl al-fatrah?
A) They will all enter Hell
B) They are all saved, even if they worshipped idols
C) They will be tested in the afterlife and some may be punished
D) They are not accountable and will enter Paradise without test

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-fatrah are all saved because they never received a clear prophetic message, and any reports suggesting punishment are either weak or refer to exceptional cases known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly rely on God's mercy for your own salvation, or do you secretly believe that your deeds make you deserving? How does the teaching that ahl al-fatrah are saved by sheer mercy challenge your sense of entitlement before God?
?
When you hear reports of punishment for certain people, do you quickly conclude that they deserved it? What does this lesson's careful handling of such reports teach you about how to think about the fate of others?
?
If God's anger is so intense on that day that He is not questioned, what does that mean for your own hope of salvation? Are you prepared to stand before a God whose actions are not subject to your approval?

Answering Quranic Objections on Acquired Knowledge
Objection-and-answer with four interpretative responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars interpret Quranic verses that seem to imply Allah acquires knowledge, and you will know the four classic responses that preserve Allah's eternal knowledge.

Core Idea
Quranic verses about Allah 'knowing' after events are metaphorical, not literal.

The Quran contains verses that, taken literally, suggest Allah learns new things from events. This contradicts the doctrine that Allah's knowledge is eternal and unchanging. In this passage, the author presents the objection and then gives four scholarly answers that explain why the apparent meaning is not intended. Understanding these answers is essential for correct interpretation of these verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and cited verses
Read the objection carefully and note the list of Quranic verses that appear to imply Allah acquires knowledge from events.
The verses are from al-Kahf, al-Baqara, Aal Imran, Muhammad, al-Anfal, and Saba'.
2
Understand the theological problem
Reflect on why the apparent meaning of these verses contradicts the Islamic doctrine of Allah's eternal, unchanging knowledge.
3
Study the four answers
Read each of the four answers in order. Notice how each answer reinterprets the verses without rejecting scripture.
The answers involve figurative attribution, eternal knowledge of future existence, metaphorical meaning, and substitution of 'knowledge' for 'seeing'.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect on the broader principle that the apparent meaning (zahir) of scripture is not always the intended meaning, especially when it conflicts with clear doctrinal foundations.
This principle is crucial in Islamic theology for reconciling apparent contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: فقد وردت في القرآن آيات كثيرة يوهم ظاهرها اكتساب الله تعالى العلم، نحو قوله سبحانه: ﴿ثُمَّ بَعَثْنَهُمْ لِنَعْلَمَ أَيُّ الْحِزْبَيْنِ أَحْصَى لِمَا لَبِثُوا أَمَدًا﴾ [الكهف: ١٢]، ألا ترى أن ظاهر الكلام يقتضي أنه تعالى إنَّما بعثهم ليحصل له هذا العلم ؟ ويرجع الأمر إلى أنه سبحانه يستفيد ببعثهم علما لم يكن حاصلا له. ونظائر هذه الآية كثيرةٌ في القرآن منها قوله في سورة البقرة: ﴿إِلَّا لِنَعْلَمَ مَن يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُولَ مِمَّن يَنقَلِبُ عَلَى عَقِبَيْهِ﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٣]، وقوله في سورة آل عمران: ﴿أَمْ حَسِبْتُمْ أَن تَدْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ وَلَمَّا يَعْلَمِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ جَهَدُوا مِنكُمْ وَيَعْلَمَ الصَّابِرِينَ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٤٢]، وقوله جلّت كلمته: ﴿إِنَّا جَعَلْنَا مَا عَلَى الْأَرْضِ زِينَةً لَهَا لِنَبْلُوَهُمْ﴾ [الكهف: ٧]، وقوله: ﴿وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم حَتَّى نَعْلَمَ الْمُجَهِدِينَ مِنكُمْ وَالصَّابِرِينَ﴾ [محمد: ۳۱]، وقوله : ﴿الآنَ خَفَّفَ اللهُ عَنكُمْ وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ فِيكُمْ ضَعْفًا﴾ [الأنفال: ٦٦]، وقوله: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لَهُ عَلَيْهِم مِّن سُلْطانِ إِلَّا لِنَعْلَمَ مَن يُؤْمِنُ بِالآخِرَةِ﴾ [سبأ: ٢١] . فالجواب أن نقول لك: إن ظاهر هذه الآيات ونحوها غير مرادٍ وقد أجاب العلماء عنها بعدة أجوبة غير الذي ذكره الشارح: أحدها: أن مراد الله تعالى أن يَعلَم الرَّسول ومَن معه مِن المؤمنين، فأسند الفعل إلى نفسه وهو يريد حزبه وأولياءه ، وذلك كما يقول الملك فعلنا كذا وفتحنا البلد الفلاني، وليس هو الفاعل، ولا الفاتح، وإنما الفاعل عُمَّاله والفاتح جيشه ، ونحن نقول الآن: فتح عمر بن الخطاب له سواد العراق . والثَّاني: أن معنى الكلام ليحصل ما هو معلوم لنا ، فيصير موجودا في الخارج، فيتعلّق علمنا بوجوده كما تعلّق به أزلا على أنَّه سيوجد، فإن معلوم الله لا يمكن أن يتعلق علمه بوجوده قبل أن يوجد ، وقد تقدم ذكر ذلك في بيان تعلق العلم. والثالث: أن العلم ههنا مجاز ، والمراد إلا لتَميُّز هؤلاء بانكشاف ما في قلوبهم من إخلاص أو نفاق ، حتى يتسنى للمؤمنين أن يوالوا منهم من يستحق الموالاة، ويعادوا منهم من يستحق المعاداة . والرابع: أنّ العلم ههنا مجاز عن الرُّؤية، والعرب تضع العلم مكان الرؤية، وتضع الرؤية مكان العلم، وقد ورد ذلك في القرآن الكريم في نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ فَعَلَ رَبُّكَ﴾ [الفجر: ٦] ، وعلم ، وشهد ، ورأى ألفاظ متعاقبة يقع بعضها موقع بعض.
For if you say: There have come in the Quran many verses whose apparent meaning suggests the acquisition of knowledge by Allah, the Exalted, such as His statement, glory be to Him: 'Then We awakened them that We might know which of the two factions was most precise in calculating the length of their stay' [al-Kahf:12]. Do you not see that the apparent meaning of the speech requires that He, the Exalted, only awakened them so that this knowledge might occur to Him? And the matter returns to the fact that He, glory be to Him, benefits from resurrecting them with knowledge that was not present for Him. And similar verses are many in the Quran, including His statement in Surat al-Baqara: 'But that We might know who follows the messenger from him who turns on his heels' [al-Baqara:143], and His statement in Surat Aal Imran: 'Or did you think that you would enter Paradise while Allah has not yet known those who strove among you and known the patient?' [Aal Imran:142], and His statement, exalted be His word: 'Indeed We have made that which is on the earth an adornment for it that We may test them' [al-Kahf:7], and His statement: 'And We will surely test you until We know the warriors among you and the patient' [Muhammad:31], and His statement: 'Now Allah has lightened your burden and known that among you is weakness' [al-Anfal:66], and His statement: 'And he had no authority over them except that We might know he who believes in the Hereafter' [Saba':21]. The answer is to say to you: The apparent meaning of these verses and similar ones is not intended, and the scholars have answered them with several answers other than what the commentator mentioned: First: That Allah, the Exalted, intended that the messenger and those with him from the believers should know, so He attributed the action to Himself while intending His party and His friends. This is like when a king says, 'We did such and such and We conquered such and such a city,' while he is not the doer nor the conqueror; rather, the doer is his officials and the conqueror is his army. And we now say, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab conquered the Sawad of Iraq.' Second: That the meaning of the speech is that what is known to us should occur, so it becomes existent in the external world, and our knowledge becomes attached to its existence as it was attached to it eternally that it will exist. For Allah's known thing cannot have His knowledge attached to its existence before it exists, and this has been mentioned previously in the explanation of the attachment of knowledge. Third: That the word 'knowledge' here is metaphorical, and the intended meaning is nothing except that these people be distinguished by the uncovering of what is in their hearts of sincerity or hypocrisy, so that the believers may befriend those who deserve friendship and enmify those who deserve enmity. Fourth: That 'knowledge' here is a metaphor for 'seeing'; the Arabs place 'knowledge' in the position of 'seeing' and place 'seeing' in the position of 'knowledge'. And that has occurred in the Noble Quran, such as His statement, the Exalted: 'Have you not seen how your Lord did?' [al-Fajr:6], and 'ilm, 'shahida, and 'ra'a are interchangeable terms, each taking the place of the other.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objection is that many Quranic verses appear to imply that Allah acquires knowledge through events, which would contradict the impossibility of acquired knowledge. The objector cites several verses: from Surat al-Kahf (12), al-Baqara (143), Aal Imran (142), al-Kahf (7), Muhammad (31), al-Anfal (66), and Saba' (21). The answer is that the apparent meaning is not intended. The author then presents four scholarly responses (ajwiba) other than what the commentator previously mentioned. First response (ahaduhā): The attribution of the action to Allah is figurative; the actual agent is the messenger or believers. Just as a king says 'We conquered' while his army conquered, so Allah attributes to Himself the actions of His chosen ones. Second response (al-thānī): The verse means that the event occurs and becomes part of our knowledge; Allah's eternal knowledge of the event's occurrence is attached to it in eternity, not as a result of the event. Third response (al-thālith): The word 'knowledge' is metaphorical (majāz); the real intended meaning is that people become distinguished by their inner states, so that believers can know whom to befriend. Fourth response (al-rābiʿ): 'Knowledge' is a metaphor for 'seeing'; in Arabic, 'knowledge' and 'seeing' are used interchangeably, as seen in the verse 'Have you not seen how your Lord did?' Thus, these verses do not imply that Allah acquires new knowledge.

Key Terms
علم مكتسب
آيات متشابهات
ظاهر
مجاز
تعلق العلم
رؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quranic verses literally mean Allah acquires new knowledge from events.
Correction: The apparent meaning is not intended; the verses are metaphorical, as explained by the four answers.

Checkpoint
Which of the four answers interprets 'knowledge' in the verses as a metaphor for 'seeing'?
A) The first answer, attributing the action to the messenger.
B) The second answer, about knowledge attached to existence.
C) The third answer, about distinguishing hearts.
D) The fourth answer, about metaphorical substitution.

Key Takeaway
The four answers show that Quranic verses seeming to imply Allah's acquired knowledge are interpreted metaphorically to uphold Allah's eternal, unchanging knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever live as if Allah is waiting to see what you will do, as if He doesn't already know your choices and outcomes? How does this expose a lack of trust in His eternal knowledge?
?
When you face trials, do you think Allah is learning about your patience or sincerity through the event? How can you remind yourself that His knowledge is complete and eternal, and that trials are for your benefit, not His discovery?
?
The scholars offered deep interpretations to protect Allah's perfection. Are there any aspects of your belief about Allah that you have accepted superficially, without examining whether they truly reflect His transcendence? Will you commit to studying His attributes more deeply?

Three Interpretations of 'خلق آدم على صورته'
Discusses three scholarly views on the pronoun in the hadith about Adam's creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three scholarly interpretations of the pronoun in the hadith 'خلق آدم على صورته' and the theological reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The hadith has three valid interpretations, all affirming divine transcendence.

This passage examines a famous hadith that might seem to imply anthropomorphism. Scholars have offered three main explanations for what 'His image' refers to. The author, Abu Raja', presents each view and adds his own insight, demonstrating how careful interpretation safeguards tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote about Abu Thawr and Ahmad
Start by reading the story of Abu Thawr's initial view and Ahmad ibn Hanbal's objection. Notice how Ahmad's question forces a clarification.
This anecdote sets the stage for the three views.
2
Identify the three scholarly views
After the anecdote, the author lists three positions on the pronoun's referent. Read each one carefully and note the key difference.
Views: (1) refers to Adam, (2) refers to the struck brother, (3) refers to Allah.
3
Analyze the author's personal interpretation
The author offers a fourth interpretation of the variant 'على صورة الرحمن'. Understand his reasoning that 'الرحمن' refers to the attribute of mercy, not Allah's essence.
This interpretation promotes compassion and avoids anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on how each view preserves divine transcendence
Consider how all three views avoid likening Allah to creation. The first view sees the image as predetermined form, the second as a moral lesson, the third as compatible with transcendence through interpretation.
The key is that none of the interpretations attribute a physical image to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
أهل السنة أنَّ أبا ثور قال في حديث: إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته» إن الضمير عائد إلى آدم ، فهجره ، فأتاه أبو ثور ، فقال أحمد أي صورة كانت لآدم يخلقه عليها ؟ فكيف تصنع بقوله: خلق الله آدم على صورة الرحمن ؟ فاعتذر إليه ، وتابَ بين يديه.
قال أبو رجاء غفر الله تعالى له ولواديه ، والحاصل : أنَّ للعلماء في مرجع الضمير في هذا الحديث ثلاثة أقوال الأول: أنَّ الضَّمير عائد إلى آدم وهو ما كان يقول به أبو ثور ، ومعناه سبحانه أوجده على الصُّورة التي اقتضى علمه أن يكون عليها عند وجوده، وهو معنى مستقيم مع هذا التأويل.
أنَّه
والثَّاني : أنَّ الضمير يعود إلى الأخ المضروب ، ومعناه أن الله تعالى خلق آدم أبا البشر على صورة هذا العبد ، وأنت أيها الضارب ابن آدم، فما ينبغي لك أن تضرب صورة أبيك، وقد يكون المراد إنكم جميعاً أولاد آدم وقد ملّكَكَ اللهُ بعض إخوتك فلا تتعاظم عليه ، كما ورد في حديث آخر: «كُلكم لآدم وآدم من تراب وفي حديث آخر: «إخوانكم خَوَلُكُمْ» وفي الحديث ما يؤيد هذا المعنى أقوى تأييد.
•
والقول الثالث: أنَّ الضمير يعود إلى الله تعالى، وهو ما كان أحمد له يقوله ، وتأويله على ما سبق ذكره ، وبقي عندي في رواية إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن» وجه آخر ، وهو: أن لا يكون المراد من «الرحمن» هو الله تعالى كما فهم أحمد رضي الله تعالى عنه ، ولكن المراد الذات المتصفة بالوصف الدال على الرحمة والمراد أن الله تعالى فَطَرَ أبناء آدم على صفة الرحمة ؛ فمَن خالف ذلك كان خارجا عن مقتضى الجبلة الإنسانية إلى صفات الحيوانية من القسوة والوحشية، نظير قوله : كل مولود يولد على الفطرة، ثم أبواه يُهَوِّدَانِه أو يُنَصِّرَانِه أو يُمَجِّسَانه» فمراده - على هذا - إثارة الشَّفَقَة على أخيه، هذا ما ظهر لي ، والله أعلم.
Section on Divine Matters. The Ahl al-Sunnah relate that Abu Thawr said regarding the hadith, 'Indeed Allah Almighty created Adam upon His image,' that the pronoun refers to Adam. So he (Ahmad) abandoned him. Then Abu Thawr came to him, and Ahmad said, 'What image did Adam have when He created him?' So how do you deal with His statement, 'Allah created Adam upon the image of the Merciful'? So he apologized to him and repented before him. Abu Raja' said, may Allah forgive him and his parents. The conclusion is that scholars have three sayings regarding the reference of the pronoun in this hadith. The first: that the pronoun refers to Adam, and this is what Abu Thawr used to say. Its meaning is that He, Exalted, brought him into existence upon the image that His knowledge required that he be upon at his existence, and this is a straightforward meaning with this interpretation. The second: that the pronoun refers to the struck brother, and its meaning is that Allah Almighty created Adam, the father of humanity, upon the image of this servant, and you, O striker, are a son of Adam, so it is not fitting for you to strike the image of your father. It may be that the intended meaning is that you are all children of Adam, and Allah has given some of your brothers authority over you, so do not be arrogant over him, as mentioned in another hadith: 'All of you are from Adam and Adam is from dust,' and in another hadith: 'Your brothers are your dependents.' The hadith supports this meaning with the strongest support. The third saying: that the pronoun refers to Allah Almighty, and this is what Ahmad used to say, and its interpretation is as previously mentioned. And there remains for me in the narration, 'Indeed Allah Almighty created Adam upon the image of the Merciful,' another aspect: that the intended meaning of 'the Merciful' is not Allah Almighty as Ahmad, may Allah be pleased with him, understood, but rather the intended meaning is the essence described with the attribute indicating mercy, and the intended meaning is that Allah Almighty created the children of Adam upon the quality of mercy. Whoever opposes that is outside the requirement of human nature and into animalistic qualities of harshness and savagery, analogous to His saying: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew or a Christian or a Magian.' So his intended meaning – upon this – is to arouse compassion for one's brother. This is what has appeared to me, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly discussion of the hadith 'خلق آدم على صورته' (Allah created Adam upon His image) and the three main views on the referent of the pronoun 'ه' in the phrase 'على صورته'. The author begins by narrating an incident involving Abu Thawr and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Abu Thawr initially held that the pronoun refers to Adam, but Ahmad objected, arguing that if so, what image did Adam have at creation, and how would one reconcile with the version that says 'على صورة الرحمن' (upon the image of the Merciful)? Abu Thawr then recanted and repented. The author then summarizes three scholarly positions: The first position, attributed to Abu Thawr, is that the pronoun refers to Adam, meaning Allah created Adam upon the specific form that Allah's knowledge decreed for him—an interpretation that is straightforward and avoids anthropomorphism. The second position is that the pronoun refers to 'the struck brother' mentioned in another hadith, meaning Allah created Adam upon the image of that particular servant. This is a moral lesson: when striking another person, one is striking the image of one's father Adam, so one should not be arrogant. The author supports this view with other hadiths urging humility. The third position is that the pronoun refers to Allah, which was Ahmad ibn Hanbal's view. The author then offers his own interpretation of a variant wording ('على صورة الرحمن'): he suggests that 'الرحمن' here does not refer to Allah's essence but to the attribute of mercy, meaning Allah created humanity inherently inclined to mercy; thus, cruelty is an unnatural deviation. This interpretation aims to promote compassion. The passage ends with the author acknowledging that this is his personal understanding, deferring to Allah's greater knowledge.

الضمير
أبو ثور
أحمد بن حنبل
صورة الرحمن
الفطرة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third view (pronoun referring to Allah) implies that Allah has a physical image.
Correction: The passage clarifies that this view does not imply anthropomorphism; it is interpreted in a manner that affirms divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the outcome of the debate between Abu Thawr and Ahmad regarding the hadith?
A) Abu Thawr maintained his position and Ahmad accepted it.
B) Ahmad convinced Abu Thawr, who apologized and repented.
C) They agreed to disagree.
D) The debate was inconclusive.

Key Takeaway
Careful interpretation of ambiguous hadiths like this one protects the doctrine of tawhid by ensuring that no physical attributes are ascribed to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith that seems to describe Allah in physical terms, do you immediately try to explain it away, or do you pause and seek guidance from trustworthy scholars? Are there any such hadith you have misinterpreted in the past? Will you repent from that error today?
?
The author concludes that cruelty is a deviation from the fitrah upon which Allah created humanity. Examine your own character: in which relationships or situations have you shown harshness instead of mercy? What specific step can you take this week to restore the merciful nature Allah has placed within you?
?
Abu Thawr repented after being corrected by Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Is there a belief about Allah or His attributes that you are currently holding onto, even though it might be flawed? Are you willing to humble yourself, seek correction, and change your understanding for the sake of tawhid?

The Ash'ari-Maturidi Difference on Promise and Threat
Commentator clarifies the scope of Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement on wa'd and wa'id.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis regarding Allah's promise and threat, and why only the threat is a point of contention.

Core Idea
Allah always fulfills His promise; the disagreement is only about His threat.

This lesson examines a subtle but important theological distinction between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools. The commentator clarifies that the apparent disagreement on both promise and threat is actually limited to the threat alone. Understanding this nuance helps avoid mischaracterizing the schools' positions on divine justice and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once to get a sense of the commentator's argument. Then read the translation side by side.
The passage is a blend of matn and commentary; focus on the commentator's own words.
2
Identify the correction
Notice that the commentator first states that the apparent meaning is that Ash'aris and Maturidis differ on both promise and threat, then immediately corrects this: the difference is only on threat.
This correction is the main teaching point.
3
Study the definitions
The passage provides clear definitions: promise (wa'd) is the report of reward upon compliance, threat (wa'id) is the report of punishment upon violation.
These definitions are standard in kalam.
4
Reflect on the difference
Ask yourself: Why would Ash'aris and Maturidis agree on promise but differ on threat? Consider how this relates to divine mercy and justice.
The commentator implies the difference is about the necessity of fulfilling the threat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَسأَلةُ الوَعْدِ وَالوَعِيدِ وَبَيَانُ الخِلاف فِيهَا. ولَمَّا اختلف الأشاعرة والماتريديَّةُ فى الوَعْدِ والوَعِيد (٢).. أشار إلى ذلك بقوله: (وَ) مِمَّا يجب شرعاً اعتقاده أنَّ الله تعالى (مُنْجِنٌ ) أي : مُعْطِ ( لِمَنْ أَرَادَ) به خيرًا (وَعْدَهُ ) (۳) الذي سبقتْ به إرادته في... قوله: (ولما اختلف الأشاعرة والماتريدية في الوعد والوعيد) ظاهره أن الخلاف في كل منهما، وليس كذلك، بل الخلاف إنما هو في الوعيد فقط، وأما الوعد فلا يتخلف باتفاق، ويمكن الجواب بأن قوله: (في الوعد والوعيد معناه: في بعضها، أو مجموعها، أي: في المسألة المترجمة بالوعد والوعيد، والخلاف فيها من حيث الثاني فقط. والوعد هو: الخبر عن الثواب عند الموافقة. والوعيد هو الخبر عن العقاب عند المخالفة. الأمير والشنواني. مفعول «أراد» في قول المصنف: ومُنْجِزُ لمن أرادَ وَعْدَهُ محذوف، وأما قوله: «وعده» = ...
The issue of promise and threat and the clarification of the difference concerning it. And when the Ash'aris and Maturidis differed concerning promise and threat (2).. he indicated that by his saying: (And) among what is legally obligatory to believe is that Allah, Exalted, (fulfills) i.e., gives (to whom He willed) good (His promise) (3) which His will preceded in... His saying: (And when the Ash'aris and Maturidis differed concerning promise and threat) its apparent meaning is that the difference is concerning both, but it is not so; rather the difference is only concerning the threat, while as for the promise, it is not subject to failure by agreement, and it can be answered that his saying: (concerning promise and threat means: concerning part of them, or the totality of them, i.e., concerning the issue entitled promise and threat, and the difference in it is from the second aspect only. And promise is: the report about reward upon compliance. And threat is: the report about punishment upon violation. Al-Amir and al-Shanwani. The object of 'willed' in the author's saying: 'fulfills to whom He willed His promise' is omitted, and as for his saying: 'His promise' = ...

Commentary
This passage introduces the theological issue of wa'd (promise) and wa'id (threat) and the difference between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools on this matter. The commentator explains that the apparent statement that they differ on both is not accurate; the difference is only concerning the threat (wa'id), meaning whether Allah necessarily fulfills His threat of punishment for sin. As for the promise (wa'd) of reward for obedience, there is no difference of opinion that Allah fulfills it. The commentator provides definitions: promise is the report of reward upon compliance, and threat is the report of punishment upon violation. The text then begins to comment on the author's line regarding fulfilling the promise to whom He wills, but the passage cuts off on the page.

Correction: The commentator clarifies that the difference is only concerning the threat (wa'id), while both schools agree that Allah fulfills His promise (wa'd).

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Moses' Request as Evidence for Ru'ya
Ahl al-Sunnah's first proof from the verse of Musa: Moses' request implies permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah use the fact that Moses asked for ru'ya as a proof for its permissibility.

Core Idea
A prophet would not ask for what is impossible.

The Mu'tazila claim that the verse of Moses proves ru'ya is impossible. But Ahl al-Sunnah turn the same verse into a proof. The first argument is straightforward: Moses, a great prophet, would not ask Allah for something that is rationally impossible. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila position
Understand the Mu'tazila argument that the verse negates ru'ya eternally. This sets the stage for the Ahl al-Sunnah response.
2
Identify the first Ahl al-Sunnah proof
Locate where the text says that Moses would not ask for something impossible. This is the core of the lesson.
Notice that the text emphasizes Moses' knowledge.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is a prophet's request considered evidence in theology? How does this refute the Mu'tazila?
Connects to the principle that prophets know what is permissible to ask.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رؤية المؤمنين ربهم سبحانه وتعالى في الآخرة
وأما عن الوجه الثاني: ـ وهو هل في السمع ما يدل على جواز رؤية العباد ربهم ؟ ـ فذهب المعتزلة إلى أنه ليس في السَّمع ما يدلُّ دلالة صريحة على أنَّ العباد يرون ربهم، بل في السَّمع ما يدلُّ على أنَّ هذه الرؤية لا تجوز عليه تعالى، ولزمهم أن يُؤوّلوا صريح القرآن الأحاديث ليوافق ما ذهبوا إليه ، وعُمدتهم في هذا الوجه قوله تعالى حكاية عن موسى : رَت أَرني أنظر إلَيْكَ قَالَ لَن تَرَننِي وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَى فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكَّا وَخَرَّ مُوسَى صَعِقَا) [الأعراف: ١٤٣] - الآية) قالوا: أجاب الله تعالى على سؤال موسى الرؤية بقوله: لَنْ تَراني) فنفى الرُّوية ، ثمَّ علَّق رؤيته على استقرار الجبل ، وهو سبحانه يعلمُ أنَّه لن يستقر ، فكأنه علقها على أمر مستحيل فتكون رؤيته سبحانه مستحيلة، حتى اضطر الزمخشري في تفسيره وفي كتبه التي صنعها في النَّحو إلى أنَّ يَدَّعي أنَّ (لَنْ) حرف يدلُّ على تأبيد النَّفي ، وخَرَّج عليه هذه الآيةَ ، وهو كلامٌ بَعثَهُ عليه هواه ومذهبه ، ولم يسبقه إليه أحدٌ من أئمة النَّحو .
وأهل السُّنَّة يقولون : إنَّ في السَّمع كثيرًا من الأحاديث الصَّحيحة والآياتِ الكريمة ما يدل صراحةً على جواز رؤية العبيد ربَّهم ، وسلَّم ببعض هذه النصوص فيما بعد، ويقولون أيضا: إنَّ هذه الآية التي جعلها المعتزلة حُجَّتهم ، وطَنْطَنَ بها الزمخشري ودَنْدَن حولها ، نقولُ: إِنَّ هذه الآية نفسُها تَدُلُّ على جواز الرؤية من عدة وجوه:
الأول: أنَّ موسى طلبها من ربه ، ولا شَكٍّ عند عاقل أنَّ موسى أدرى بما يجوز في حقه طلبها تعالى وما لا يجوز من المعتزلة ؛ فلو كان يعلم أنَّ رؤية العباد ربَّهم مستحيلة لما استساغ لنفسه أن يطلبها .
الوجه الثاني: أنَّ الله تعالى نفى الرُّؤية التي طلبها ، ولم يقل له: كيف تطلب منّي ما لا يجوز في حقي؟ أو نحو ذلك مما يدل على خطَاً موسى إن قُدِّرَ ، وأهل اللسان العربي يعلمون من أسلوب العرب ومحاوراتهم في كلامهم أنَّ المتكلّم لا ينفي شيئًا إِلَّا حيثُ يُجوِّزُ ثبوته ، نعني أنَّه لا يقول قائل : لم يضرب محمد عليَّا ، إلا في مقام يجوز أن يكون محمد قد ضرب عليًّا، فأما حيث لا يجوز ثبوت الشيء للشيء فإن المتكلمون من العرب، بل ومن غير العرب من الأمم لا ينفون ذلك الشيء ؛ فلم نسمع أحدا قال لآخر: «لم ينطق هذا الجبل» ولا «لم يصعد هذا الحمار هذه الشجرة» ولو أنَّ قائلا قال ذلك لَعَدَّه النَّاس هازلا هاذيا ، فلما قال الله تعالى: (لَنْ تَرَاني) علمنا بمقتضى عُرف اللّسان والأسلوب العربي أنَّ الرُّؤية في نفسها أمر جائز . والوجه الثالث: أنه سبحانه علق حصول الرُّؤية في آخر الآية على أمر جائز في نفسه وهو استقرار الجبل، بل هو من حيث ذاته أقرب من صيرورته دَكَّا، وكلُّ أمرٍ يعلّق حصوله على أمر جائز فهو جائز ، وأمَّا ادّعاء المعتزلة أنَّ استقرار الجبل مستحيل لكونه تعالى قد علم أنَّه لا يستقر ، فهو مما لا يُخْرِجُه عن كونه في نفسه جائزاً
The seeing of the believers of their Lord, Exalted and Majestic, in the Hereafter. As for the second aspect: whether in the revelation (sam') there is evidence for the permissibility of the servants seeing their Lord. The Mu'tazila held that there is nothing in the revelation that clearly indicates that the servants see their Lord; rather, there is in the revelation what indicates that this vision is not permissible for Him, Exalted. And they are obliged to interpret the clear Quranic verses and hadiths to agree with what they went to. Their mainstay in this aspect is the saying of Allah Almighty narrating from Moses: 'Lord, show me (that) I may look at You.' He said: 'You will not see Me, but look at the mountain; if it remains in its place, then you will see Me.' So when his Lord manifested to the mountain, He made it level and Moses fell down unconscious. (7:143) — the verse. They said: Allah Almighty answered Moses' request for vision with His saying: 'You will not see Me' (lan taranī). So He negated the vision, then attached His vision to the stability of the mountain, and He Almighty knows that it will not remain, so it is as if He attached it to an impossible thing, thus His vision, Exalted, is impossible. So much so that al-Zamakhshari, in his commentary and in the books he authored in grammar, was forced to claim that (lan) is a particle that indicates eternal negation, and he deduced this verse accordingly. This is speech that his whim and sect caused him to utter, and no one among the authorities of grammar preceded him in this. And Ahl al-Sunnah say: In the revelation there are many authentic hadiths and noble verses that clearly indicate the permissibility of the servants seeing their Lord, and they submit to some of these texts later. And they also say: This very verse that the Mu'tazila made their argument, and with which al-Zamakhshari made a noise and hummed around, we say: This very verse itself indicates the permissibility of vision from several aspects: The first: That Moses asked for it from his Lord, and there is no doubt for a rational person that Moses was more knowledgeable about what is permissible for him to ask his Lord, Exalted, and what is not permissible — from the Mu'tazila. So if he knew that the servants' seeing their Lord is impossible, he would not have allowed himself to ask for it. The second aspect: That Allah Almighty negated the vision that he asked for, and He did not say to him: 'How do you ask from Me what is not permissible for Me?' or the like, which would indicate Moses' error if it were supposed. And the people of the Arabic language know from the style of the Arabs and their conversations in their speech that the speaker does not negate something except where he permits its existence. I mean, a speaker does not say 'Muhammad did not hit Ali' except in a context where it is possible that Muhammad hit Ali. But where the existence of a thing for a thing is not permissible, the speakers among the Arabs, and even among non-Arabs of the nations, do not negate that thing. So we have not heard anyone say to another: 'This mountain did not speak' nor 'This donkey did not climb this tree.' And if a speaker said that, people would consider him a jester and a babbler. So when Allah Almighty said: (Lan taranī), we know by the convention of the tongue and the Arabic style that vision in itself is permissible. And the third aspect: That He, Exalted, attached the occurrence of vision at the end of the verse to something that is permissible in itself, namely the stability of the mountain. Indeed, it is in itself closer to becoming level. And every matter whose occurrence is attached to a permissible matter is permissible. As for the Mu'tazila's claim that the stability of the mountain is impossible because He Almighty knows that it will not remain, that does not remove it from being permissible in itself.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage addresses the second aspect (al-wajh al-thani) of the discussion on ru'ya: whether the revealed sources (al-samʿ) indicate the permissibility of seeing Allah. The Mu'tazila argue that the verse of Moses (7:143) actually proves the impossibility of ru'ya. They interpret 'lan taranī' as an eternal negation, and claim that Allah attached the vision to an impossible condition (the mountain remaining stable) to show ru'ya is impossible. The author notes that Zamakhshari even claimed that 'lan' indicates eternal negation in grammar, a view he innovated. Then Ahl al-Sunnah respond with three proofs from the same verse demonstrating that ru'ya is permissible. The first proof: Moses, a great prophet, asked for ru'ya, and he would not ask for something impossible. The second proof: Allah's negation 'lan taranī' is only meaningful if ru'ya is possible in itself, because negation implies the possibility of existence in the linguistic convention of the Arabs. The author gives examples: one would not say 'this mountain did not speak' because speech for a mountain is impossible. So Allah's negation indicates that ru'ya is possible but will not occur at that moment. The third proof: The condition of the mountain's stability is something permissible in itself (i.e., it could happen), and attaching ru'ya to a permissible condition indicates that ru'ya itself is permissible. The Mu'tazila's argument that Allah's knowledge makes it impossible is not relevant because the condition is intrinsically possible. Thus, the verse actually supports the Ahl al-Sunnah position.

Key Terms
الرؤية
طلب
موسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Moses was mistaken to ask for ru'ya, implying ru'ya is impossible.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunnah hold that Moses, as a prophet, knew that ru'ya is possible; otherwise he would not have asked.

Checkpoint
According to the first Ahl al-Sunnah proof, why does Moses' request for ru'ya prove its permissibility?
A) Because Moses was granted the vision later.
B) Because a prophet would not ask for something impossible.
C) Because the verse uses the word 'lan'.
D) Because the mountain remained stable.

Key Takeaway
Moses' request for ru'ya shows that ru'ya is fundamentally possible, otherwise he would not have asked.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever hesitate to ask Allah for something because you think it might be impossible? How does Moses' example challenge that hesitation, and what will you ask Him for today that you've been afraid to request?
?
When you read that Moses asked to see Allah, does your heart long for that vision? What practical steps can you take this week to increase your desire to meet your Lord, rather than being satisfied with this world?
?
Think of a time you doubted that a request to Allah was permissible or appropriate. Did that doubt stop you from asking? How can Moses' confidence in what is permissible change the way you approach Allah in your next dua?

Linguistic and Conditional Arguments for Ru'ya
Ahl al-Sunnah's second and third proofs: linguistic negation and conditional attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two additional proofs from the verse of Musa: the linguistic principle of negation and the conditional attachment to a permissible thing.

Core Idea
Negation proves possibility; condition proves possibility.

Ahl al-Sunnah offer two more sophisticated arguments from the same verse. First, they analyse the grammar of negation: when Arabs negate something, they imply it could happen. Second, they note that Allah attached ru'ya to a condition that is intrinsically possible, showing ru'ya itself is possible. This lesson explores these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof about negation
Understand the linguistic principle: the Arabs only negate what is possible to affirm. Allah's negation 'lan taranī' therefore implies ru'ya is possible.
The example of the mountain not speaking is given to illustrate.
2
Read the third proof about the condition
Allah says 'if the mountain remains, you will see Me.' The condition is possible, so the result (ru'ya) is possible.
Contrast with the Mu'tazila claim that the condition is impossible due to foreknowledge.
3
Reflect on the refutation
How do these two proofs together refute the Mu'tazila reliance on the same verse?
The verse actually supports Ahl al-Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رؤية المؤمنين ربهم سبحانه وتعالى في الآخرة

The seeing of the believers of their Lord, Exalted and Majestic, in the Hereafter. Commentary
This passage addresses the second aspect (al-wajh al-thani) of the discussion on ru'ya: whether the revealed sources (al-samʿ) indicate the permissibility of seeing Allah. The Mu'tazila argue that the verse of Moses (7:143) actually proves the impossibility of ru'ya. They interpret 'lan taranī' as an eternal negation, and claim that Allah attached the vision to an impossible condition (the mountain remaining stable) to show ru'ya is impossible. The author notes that Zamakhshari even claimed that 'lan' indicates eternal negation in grammar, a view he innovated. Then Ahl al-Sunnah respond with three proofs from the same verse demonstrating that ru'ya is permissible. The first proof: Moses, a great prophet, asked for ru'ya, and he would not ask for something impossible. The second proof: Allah's negation 'lan taranī' is only meaningful if ru'ya is possible in itself, because negation implies the possibility of existence in the linguistic convention of the Arabs. The author gives examples: one would not say 'this mountain did not speak' because speech for a mountain is impossible. So Allah's negation indicates that ru'ya is possible but will not occur at that moment. The third proof: The condition of the mountain's stability is something permissible in itself (i.e., it could happen), and attaching ru'ya to a permissible condition indicates that ru'ya itself is permissible. The Mu'tazila's argument that Allah's knowledge makes it impossible is not relevant because the condition is intrinsically possible. Thus, the verse actually supports the Ahl al-Sunnah position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'lan' in 'lan taranī' indicates eternal and absolute negation of ru'ya, as claimed by al-Zamakhshari.
Correction: Linguistic scholars note that 'lan' does not inherently imply eternity; the context and the fact that Moses asked show the negation is temporary.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, why does Allah's statement 'lan taranī' actually support the possibility of ru'ya?
A) Because 'lan' indicates that the negation is temporary.
B) Because the Arabs only negate things when their existence is possible.
C) Because Moses was ignorant of the impossibility.
D) Because the mountain's stability is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The verse of Moses actually supports the possibility of ru'ya through its linguistic and conditional structure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Lan taranī' in the verse, did you ever assume it was an absolute denial of seeing Allah forever? How does the Arabic linguistic principle of negation force you to reconsider your interpretation of other Quranic negations about Allah?
?
If Allah's speech carries such precise meaning that every negation points to possibility, how carefully do you weigh your own words when you speak about Allah or His attributes? Will you read His verses with more attention from now on?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted that Allah's foreknowledge makes an event impossible. Have you ever used Allah's knowledge as an excuse to avoid striving, thinking it was already impossible? How does this lesson challenge that mindset?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Scriptural Objection to Ru'ya
Sanusi answers the Mu'tazilite scriptural objection from the Quranic verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazilite scriptural objection to seeing Allah by showing that the Quranic verse is in the context of praise and that other scriptural requests were due to obstinacy, not impossibility.

Core Idea
The Quranic 'No vision can grasp Him' is praise, not absolute negation.

The Mu'tazilites used several scriptural arguments to deny the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife. Their strongest proof was the verse 'No vision can grasp Him.' Sanusi explains that this verse is presented in a context of praise, not as a categorical denial. He also addresses other scriptural examples to reinforce that such requests were due to obstinacy, not impossibility. In this lesson, we examine the objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage combines the objection and the answer in a compressed form.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite scriptural objection
Find the verse they used as their strongest proof. Notice how they formulated the argument: the negation of 'idrak' (grasping) by sight is presented in the context of praise, implying it is a permanent negation.
The objection is that this verse proves ru'ya is impossible in the afterlife.
3
Understand the answer: the context of praise
Sanusi states that the negation is 'wārid mawrida al-tamadduh' (entered the context of praise). This means the verse is praising Allah's transcendence, not categorically denying that He can be seen.
This is the key refutation: the verse does not address rational possibility.
4
Consider the additional examples and the answer from al-Mahalli
The passage mentions other scriptural examples where people requested to see Allah and were punished. The answer is that these requests were due to obstinacy (ta'annut), not because the requested (ru'ya) is impossible.
This reinforces that the impossibility is not inherent in the act of seeing Allah.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Ask yourself: Does this passage prove that ru'ya is rationally possible? Yes, because the objection is shown to be based on a misunderstanding of the Quranic context.
The lesson shows how scriptural objections are answered by careful interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتمسكوا أيضا بشبه سمعية (۳)، أقواها قوله تعالى: وَلَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ [الأنعام: ۱۰۳]. وتقريرُ التّمسُّك به الذي تَعرَّض لجوابه: أنَّ نفي إدراكه تعالى بالبصر .. وارد مَورِدَ التَّمدح، مُدْرَج في أثناء (۳) قوله: ( بشبه سمعية) منها : أَرنَا اللَّهَ جَهْرَةً فَأَخَذَتْهُمُ الصَّعِقَةُ) [النساء: ١٥٣] وآية: أَوْ نَرَى رَبَّنا لَقَدِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فِي أَنفُسِهِمْ وَعَتَوْ عُنُوًا كَبِيرًا وأجيب كما في المحلي: بأن ذلك للتّعنت في الطلب لا لكون المطلوب محالا . الأمير .
They also adhered to scriptural doubts, the strongest of which is His saying the Exalted: 'No vision can grasp Him, but He grasps all vision' (al-An'am 103). And the formulation of adherence to it, which [the author] undertook to answer, is that the negation of grasping Him by sight is presented in the context of praise, inserted in the midst of speech. (Footnote 3) His saying: 'with scriptural doubts' includes: 'Show us Allah openly' so the thunderbolt seized them (al-Nisa 153) and the verse 'We wish to see our Lord' they were arrogant and greatly defiant. And the answer, as in al-Mahalli, is that that was due to obstinacy in the request, not because the requested is impossible. al-Amir.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazilite scriptural objection against ru'ya, particularly the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' (No vision can grasp Him). The author notes that they use this as a proof that ru'ya is impossible. The answer, which the author indicates he is about to give, is that the negation in the verse is presented in a context of praise (tamadduh) and is inserted within speech that has its own context—it does not categorically negate ru'ya. The author then, through the footnote, adds other scriptural examples like the request of the Israelites to see Allah, which resulted in punishment. The answer given, as cited from al-Mahalli, is that such requests were due to obstinacy (ta'annut) and not because the requested (ru'ya) is impossible in itself. Thus, the verse does not prove that ru'ya is rationally impossible.

سمعيات (sam'iyyat)
تعدد (tamadduh)
تعنت (ta'annut)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quranic verse 'No vision can grasp Him' absolutely negates the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife.
Correction: The verse is in the context of praise (tamadduh) and does not preclude rational possibility; other scriptural examples show that requests to see Allah were punished due to obstinacy, not because the act is impossible.

Checkpoint

B) Because the negation is in the context of praise, not a categorical denial.
C) Because it refers only to worldly vision.
D) Because the verse is metaphorical and not literal.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' does not negate the rational possibility of seeing Allah; it is a statement of praise that does not preclude ru'ya in the afterlife.

Dreams and the Limits of Solitary Visions in Legal Rulings
Psychological principle and legal case about dreams vs. tawātur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a dream, even if it appears to come from the Prophet, cannot override a ruling established by mass transmission (tawātur), and the psychological basis for vivid dreams.

Core Idea
Dreams are solitary strands; they cannot break the chain of mass-transmitted truths.

This lesson explores a fascinating story from Islamic scholarship that clarifies the role of dreams in legal matters. We begin with a psychological observation about how intense focus can make the absent seem present, setting the stage for a real case where a man's dream instruction about treasure was overruled by the principle of tawātur. By the end, you'll grasp why dreams, however vivid, are not a source of legislation when they contradict established mass-transmitted proofs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the psychological principle
Read the opening lines about 'states making the absent present' and reflect on how deep preoccupation can create a vivid sense of presence. This explains why dreams can feel so real.
This is a common experience; everyone can relate to it.
2
Read the story of the man and the dream
Read the story (fā’ida) carefully: a man sees the Prophet in a dream who tells him about a treasure and that no khums is due. The man acts on it.
3
Analyze al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam's ruling
The scholar rules that the man must pay khums because the obligation is established by tawātur (mass transmission), while the dream is only āḥād (solitary). This is the core point.
Tawātur is stronger than any solitary report, including a dream.
4
Consider the analogy with Eid and Ramadan
The passage extends the principle: if someone dreams that tomorrow is Eid or Ramadan, he must rely on conventional signs like moon sighting, not the dream.
This reinforces that dreams do not override established methods.
5
Summarize the lesson's teaching
Reflect on the balance between personal spiritual experiences and the collective, mass-transmitted knowledge of the Sharia.
Dreams can be true but are not legislative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رؤية النبي لربه في الدنيا ليلة الإسراء والمعراج . الأحوال تجعل الغائب كالشاهد ، حتى إذا كثر اشتغال الشخص بشيء واستحضاره له صار كأنه حاضر بين يديه كما هو معلوم بالوجدان لكل أحد الشنواني . فائدة: حكي أن رجلا رأى النبي الله في المنام يقول له : في المكان الفلاني ركاز ذهب، خذه ولا خُمس عليك ، فذهب وأخذهنَّ ثم استفتى العلماء؛ فقال العز بن عبد السلام: أخرج الخُمْسَ فقد ثبت بالتواتر ، وقصارى رؤيتك الآحاد ، ومنه أن يقول له: غدا العيد أو رمضان ، فيعوّل على العلامات المُقررة . الشنواني .
The Prophet's seeing of his Lord in this world on the night of the Night Journey and Ascension. States make the absent like the present, such that when a person's preoccupation with something and his bringing it to mind increases, it becomes as if it is present before him, as is known by experience for everyone, al-Shanwani. Benefit: It is narrated that a man saw the Prophet of Allah in a dream saying to him: 'In such and such place there is a treasure of gold, take it and no khums (one-fifth tax) is due on you,' so he went and took it, then he sought a legal opinion from the scholars; al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam said: 'Pay the khums, for it has been established by tawātur (mass transmission), and at most your vision is āḥād (solitary),' and from this is if someone says to him: 'Tomorrow is Eid or Ramadan,' then one relies on the established signs. Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage begins with a heading: 'The Prophet's seeing of his Lord in this world on the night of the Night Journey and Ascension,' referring to the well-known incident of Mi‘rāj. Then it explains a psychological principle: strong emotional states can make the absent seem present, so when a person is deeply absorbed in thinking about something, it appears as if it is before him, as everyone knows from personal experience. This is a comment by al-Shanwani. Then the author presents a 'benefit' (fā’ida): a story of a man who saw the Prophet in a dream, who told him about a hidden treasure of gold and that no khums (one-fifth tax) is due on it. The man took the treasure and then asked scholars for a ruling. Al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam (a famous Shafi‘i scholar) responded that he must pay the khums because the obligation to pay khums on buried treasure is established by tawātur (mass-transmitted evidence), while the man's dream is only solitary (āḥād) and cannot override the established ruling. Similarly, if someone dreams that tomorrow is Eid or Ramadan, he should rely on the conventional signs (like sighting of the moon), not just the dream. This lesson emphasizes that dreams are not a source of legislation when they contradict clear, mass-transmitted proofs.

Key Terms
منام
تواتر
آحاد
خمس
ركاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a dream instruction from the Prophet is binding and must be followed even if it contradicts established rulings.
Correction: This story shows that dreams are solitary (āḥād) and cannot override rulings established by mass transmission (tawātur), such as the obligation of khums on treasure.

Checkpoint
According to the story, why did al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam rule that the man must pay khums despite the dream's instruction otherwise?
A) Because dreams are invalid.
B) Because the obligation of khums on treasure is established by tawātur, and a solitary dream cannot overturn it.
C) Because the man was lying.
D) Because the Prophet cannot be seen in dreams.

Key Takeaway
Dreams are not a source of binding legal rulings when they contradict mass-transmitted evidence; they remain solitary reports (āḥād) that cannot overturn established knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been so convinced by a personal experience, intuition, or dream that you dismissed clear evidence from the Quran and Sunnah? When will you humble yourself to submit to the mass-transmitted truth, even if it costs you something you desired?
?
The man in the story sought a scholar's opinion after acting on his dream. In a conflict between your feelings and established Islamic rulings, do you run to ask the scholars, or do you justify your desires? What treasure are you holding onto that needs the 'khums' of submission?
?
What would it take for you to abandon a comforting belief or practice because it contradicts tawātur? Are you ready to accept that your personal spiritual experiences, no matter how vivid, cannot override the collective knowledge of the Ummah?
