The Rank of Angels Relative to Prophets
The author states that angels' rank follows prophets' and specifies the chief angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general principle that angels' rank follows prophets' and the specific exception for chief angels.

Core Idea
Angels outrank all humans except prophets, but only the archangels sit directly beneath prophets in detail.

This passage clarifies a key aspect of Islamic angelology: the hierarchy of creation. While prophets hold the highest rank, angels come next. But the author introduces a nuance: it is not all angels equally; the great archangels occupy that immediate next position. Understanding this hierarchy helps avoid confusion about the relative merits of angels and saints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that the author uses the phrase 'in general' (في الجملة) and then 'in detail' (على التفصيل).
2
Identify the general rule and qualification
The passage states that the rank of angels follows prophets in general, and that angels are better than non-prophet humans. Then it specifies that in detail, only the chief angels are next to prophets.
3
Reflect on why the author mentions Abu Bakr and Umar
By mentioning the greatest saints, the author emphasizes that even the best humans (other than prophets) are below angels. This reinforces the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ أنَّ رُتبة الملائكةِ تَلي رُتبة الأنبياء في الفَضْل] (وَبَعْدَهُم) أي: وبعد الأنبياء في الفضيلة (مَلَائِكة) اللهِ (ذِي الفَضْلِ) فمرتبتهم تلي مرتبة الأنبياء عليهم السَّلام في الجملة ؛ فالملائكة - ولو غير رُسل - أفضل مِن غير الأنبياء من البشر ولو كان وليا ؛ كأبي بكر وعمر وإنما قلنا: في الجملة» لأنَّ الذي يلي الأنبياء من الملائكة على التفصيل « إِنَّما هو رؤساؤهم، كجبريل وميكائيل وإسرافيل وعزرائيل.
Explanation that the rank of angels follows the rank of prophets in merit: (And after them) meaning: after the prophets in virtue (angels) of God (possessor of bounty), so their rank follows the rank of the prophets, peace be upon them, in general; so the angels - even if not messengers - are better than non-prophets among humans, even if he is a saint, like Abu Bakr and 'Umar. And we only said: in general, because those who follow the prophets among the angels in detail are only their leaders, such as Jibril, Mika'il, Israfil, and 'Azra'il.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification. It explains the general principle that the rank of angels comes after the rank of prophets in terms of virtue. The author clarifies that this is a general rule: angels, even those who are not messengers, are superior to any human who is not a prophet, including saints like Abu Bakr and 'Umar. However, he qualifies this by stating that when speaking in detail, only the chief angels—Jibril, Mika'il, Israfil, and 'Azra'il—are immediately after the prophets in rank. The author uses the phrase 'in general' to indicate that the overall hierarchy places all angels above non-prophet humans, but the specific ranking among angels themselves places the archangels in the highest position next to the prophets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All angels are equal in rank to prophets or that some humans can be equal to angels.
Correction: Angels as a whole are below prophets but above all other humans. However, only the archangels are immediately below prophets; other angels are still above non-prophet humans.

Key Takeaway
Angels overall follow prophets in merit, but the chief angels specifically are the ones directly beneath prophets.

Definition and Attributes of Angels
Definition of angels and enumeration of their attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of angels as subtle luminous beings with specific attributes and roles, and why they are not described as male or female.

Core Idea
Angels are luminous bodies, genderless, and constantly obedient to God.

In this passage, the author defines angels by describing their physical nature, capabilities, and roles. He emphasizes that they are created from light, have no gender, and are completely devoted to worshipping Allah. This lesson unpacks each attribute mentioned.

There are at least eight distinct points.

This ties to a common misunderstanding.

The reality of the angels, jinn, and devils. Commentary
This passage defines angels by stating their reality and attributes. First, it gives the heading covering angels, jinn, and devils, but the description is limited to angels. Angels are described as subtle (لطيفة) luminous bodies, meaning they have a delicate, non-physical form made of light. They have the power to take on various shapes. They are complete in knowledge and ability to perform difficult tasks (which are not difficult for them). Their constant occupation is obedience (الطاعات), and they dwell mostly in the heavens. Their roles include being messengers to prophets and trustees of revelation. They constantly glorify God without pause. They are completely obedient, never disobeying God. They are not described as male or female because there is no evidence for such.

The Nature of Angels: Luminous Bodies Without Gender
Commentary defining angels and explaining their attributes and gender ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Sunni definition of angels: their subtle luminous bodies, their attributes, and the ruling on describing them with gender.

Core Idea
Angels are real, genderless, luminous beings in constant obedience.

This passage from the commentary establishes the fundamental Islamic belief about angels. It defines their nature as subtle luminous bodies, lists their attributes, and addresses the critical issue of gender assignment. Understanding this clarifies the unique status of angels as sinless messengers of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the source carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview, then read the literal translation. Notice how the commentator begins with a definition and then elaborates through footnotes.
The footnotes are numbered and each addresses a specific attribute or ruling.
2
Identify the definition
Locate the phrase 'أجسام لطيفة نورانية' and understand that angels are described as subtle and luminous bodies. This is their essential nature.
Subtlety means they are fine in constitution and do not crowd.
3
Analyze the attributes
List the key attributes: ability to take different forms, perfect knowledge and power for difficult actions, their concern is obedience, their dwelling is the heavens, they are messengers and trustees, they glorify continuously without tiring.
These attributes distinguish angels from other created beings.
4
Understand the gender rule
Read the final part about gender. The passage states angels are not described as male or female due to lack of evidence. It also gives rulings for those who do describe them as male (sinful) or female (disbelief).
This guards against a common misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حقيقة الملائكة والجن والشياطين
والملائكة أجسام لطيفة نورانية، قادرة على التشكل بأشكال مختلفة كاملة في العلم والقدرة على الأفعال الشاقة، شأنها الطاعات، ومسكنها السموات، هم رسل الله إلى أنبيائه عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وأمناؤه على وحيه، يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون، لا يعصون الله ما أمرهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون، لا يوصفون بذكورة ولا بأنوثة، لعدم دليل على ذلك.
(1) قوله: (لطيفة) من اللطافة، أي: رقة القوام، ولذا لا تتزاحم، فقد ورد أن الله ملكا يملأ ثلث الأرض، وملكا يملأ ثلثي الأرض، وملكا يملأ الكون كله، فإذا قيل: إذا ملاً الكون كله فأين يكون غيره؟ قلنا: الأنوار لا تتزاحم، ألا ترى أنه لو وضع سراج في البيت ملأه نورا، ولو أتينا بعدُ بألفي سراج وسع البيت أنوارها. الشنواني.
(2) قوله: (الشاقة) أي: الشاقة على غيرهم، وأما عليهم فليست شاقة، ولذا كان تسبيحهم بمنزلة النفس لنا. الشنواني.
(3) قوله: (ومسكنها السموات) أي غالبا لأن الملائكة علوية وسفلية، والعلوية سكان السموات، والسفلية سكان الأرض. الشنواني.
(4) قوله: (يسبحون الليل والنهار) هذه كناية عن الدوام، وإلا فالسموات ليس فيها ليل ولا نهار. الشنواني.
(5) ومن وصفهم بذكورة لا يكفر، قال الأمير: لكنه فاسق متقول، ومن وصفهم بالأنوثة فإنه يكفر بلا خلاف لمعارضتها لقوله تعالى: {وَجَعَلُوا الْمَلَائِكَةَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عِبَادُ الرَّحْمَٰنِ إِنَاثًا} [الزخرف: 19] وأولى من قال أنهم خناثى، لمزيد التنقيص الأمير والشنواني.
The reality of angels, jinn, and devils. And the angels are subtle luminous bodies, capable of taking on different forms, perfect in knowledge and power for difficult actions, their concern is obedience, and their dwelling is the heavens. They are the messengers of Allah to His prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, and His trustees over His revelation. They glorify night and day without tiring; they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded. They are not described as male or female, due to the absence of evidence for that. (1) His saying: (subtle) from subtlety, meaning fineness of constitution, hence they do not crowd. For it has been reported that there is an angel filling a third of the earth, an angel filling two-thirds of the earth, and an angel filling the entire universe. If it is said: when it fills the entire universe, where does other exist? We say: lights do not crowd. Do you not see that if a lamp is placed in a house it fills it with light, and if we later bring two thousand lamps the house accommodates their lights. Al-Shanwani. (2) His saying: (difficult) meaning difficult for others. As for them, it is not difficult. Hence their glorification is like breathing for us. Al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (and their dwelling is the heavens) meaning for the most part, because angels are upper and lower, and the upper ones are inhabitants of the heavens, and the lower ones are inhabitants of the earth. Al-Shanwani. (4) His saying: (they glorify night and day) is a metaphor for continuity; otherwise the heavens have no night or day. Al-Shanwani. (5) Whoever describes them as male does not disbelieve; al-Amir said: but he is a wicked fabricator. And whoever describes them as female disbelieves without dispute, because it contradicts His statement: {And they have made the angels, who are the servants of the Most Merciful, females} [Al-Zukhruf: 19]. And more deserving [of disbelief] is he who says they are hermaphrodites, due to increased degradation. Al-Amir and Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage defines angels and explains their key attributes. The definition begins by stating that angels are 'lute bodies' (ajsam latifa) meaning fine or subtle in constitution, and 'luminous' (nuraniyya) – made of light. They have the ability to take on different forms, and are perfect in knowledge and power, enabling them to perform difficult actions. Their concern is obedience, and their dwelling is the heavens. They serve as Allah's messengers to prophets and trustees of His revelation. They glorify Allah continuously without tiring and are sinless, never disobeying. Importantly, they are not described as male or female because there is no evidence for such descriptions. The footnotes further elaborate: (1) The subtlety ('lutf') means fineness of substance, so angels do not crowd; multiple powerful lights can coexist in the same space, like many lamps lighting a house. (2) The 'difficult' actions are difficult for others but not for angels; their glorification is effortless for them. (3) Their dwelling is generally the heavens, but there are also earth-dwelling angels. (4) 'Glorifying night and day' is a metaphor for perpetual worship, as the heavens have no night or day cycle. (5) The description of angels as male does not cause disbelief but is sinful; describing them as female is disbelief because it contradicts the Quran (43:19); describing them as hermaphrodites is even worse. This passage thus establishes the orthodox Sunni position on the nature of angels.

Key Terms
الملائكة
أجسام لطيفة
نورانية
التسبيح
لا يوصفون بذكورة ولا بأنوثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe angels have gender, often considering them female.
Correction: Angels have no gender; the absence of evidence and Quranic verses (43:19) show that describing them as female is disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are angels not described as male or female?
A) Because they are purely spiritual and have no bodies.
B) Because there is no evidence (dalīl) for that.
C) Because they are neither male nor female in any sense.
D) Because they are created from light and have no reproductive organs.

Key Takeaway
Angels are created beings of light, sinless, genderless, and in perpetual worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels never tire of glorifying Allah, night and day. But you—when does your worship feel like a heavy chore? What would it take for your obedience to become as natural as breathing? Will you ask Allah for that ease today?
?
You just learned that describing angels as male or female is either sinful or disbelief. But have you, even unconsciously, imagined angels with gender? How does this passage confront that mental image? What will you do to conform your belief exactly to the revelation?
?
The angels are sinless and never disobey. You, however, have chosen disobedience knowingly. What does that reveal about your will? Are you content with that, or will you now beg Allah for the strength to obey like the angels do?

Definition of Naskh and the Eternity of the Prophet's Shari'ah
Defines naskh linguistically and technically, and proves the permanence of the Prophet's Shari'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the technical meaning of naskh and why the Shari'ah of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is permanent and not subject to abrogation.

Core Idea
Naskh lifts a ruling with new evidence, but the final Shari'ah cannot be superseded.

This lesson introduces the concept of naskh (abrogation) from both linguistic and technical perspectives. We then see how the author applies this definition to establish that the Prophet's Shari'ah continues until the Day of Resurrection, supported by Quran and Hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style: definition followed by argument.
2
Understand the two definitions of naskh
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions. Note how the technical definition adds the condition of evidence.
The linguistic definition is broader; the technical is specific to Islamic law.
3
Grasp the argument for permanence
Follow the reasoning: the Shari'ah of the Prophet lasts until time itself ends, because no future abrogating law can come, and the Quran and Hadith confirm its finality.
The proof combines rational inconceivability with textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنسخ لغة: الإزالة والنقل، واصطلاحا: رفع حكم شرعي بدليل شرعي. فشرع نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم مستمر حتى الزمان ينسخ أي: حتى ينقضي الزمان ويزول بحضور القيامة، لعدم تصور الآتي بما يكون به النسخ، وعدم قبول زمان من الأزمنة المستقبلة لوقوع ذلك فيه؛ لقوله تعالى: {إِنَّ الدِّينَ عِندَ اللَّهِ الْإِسْلَامُ} {وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ} ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا تزال هذه الأمة قائمة على أمر الله تعالى - يعني الدين الحق - لا يضرهم من خالفهم حتى يأتي أمر الله».
Abrogation linguistically is removal and transfer, and terminologically: the lifting of a legislative ruling by a legislative evidence. So the law of our Prophet ﷺ is continuous until time is abrogated, i.e., until time passes away and ceases by the arrival of the Resurrection, due to the inconceivability of [any future] coming with that by which abrogation occurs, and the non-acceptance of any future time for the occurrence of that; because of His saying تعالى: {Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam} {And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him} and because of his saying عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'This ummah will continue to be steadfast upon the command of Allah تعالى - meaning the true religion - not harmed by those who oppose them until the command of Allah comes'.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage defines the term naskh (abrogation) both linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it means removal or transfer. Technically, it means the lifting of a shari' ruling by another shari' evidence. The author then applies this concept to the Shari'ah of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ. He states that this Shari'ah is continuous and will not be abrogated until the end of time itself (the Day of Resurrection). The reason given is that there is no future revelation to abrogate it, as no time remains that could accept a new abrogating law. This is supported by two Quranic verses from Surah Al-Imran, which declare that Islam is the only acceptable religion, implying that no other law can supersede it. Additionally, a hadith affirms that the Muslim community will persist upon the truth until Allah's command (the Hour) arrives, indicating the permanence of this Shari'ah.

Key Terms
النسخ (naskh)
الإزالة (izāla)
النقل (naql)
رفع حكم شرعي (raf' hukm shar'ī)
دليل شرعي (dalīl shar'ī)
شريعة (sharī'a)
دوام (dawām)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think naskh means the ruling itself is removed from existence, or that the Prophet's Shari'ah could be abrogated by another prophet.
Correction: Naskh only lifts the applicability of a ruling, and the Prophet's Shari'ah is final; no further abrogation is possible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the technical definition of naskh?
A) Removal and transfer
B) Lifting of a legislative ruling by a legislative evidence
C) The end of time
D) Change of a ruling without evidence

Key Takeaway
Naskh is the lifting of a ruling by another evidence, and the Shari'ah of the Prophet ﷺ is final and eternal until the end of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Islam is the only acceptable religion until the end of time, are you actively conveying its truth to those around you, or are you silent out of comfort? What would change if you truly felt the weight of this finality?
?
The Shari'ah of the Prophet is permanent and cannot be abrogated. Yet, is there any command of Allah that you have treated as outdated or 'for a different time' in your own life? What would it mean for you to accept every ruling as eternally binding on you personally?
?
This lesson proves that no new revelation will come to change God's law. Does your heart find peace in that certainty, or does it secretly wish for an easier path? What does your answer reveal about the state of your iman and your submission to Allah's wisdom?

Abrogation of Previous Scriptures by Islam
Sanusi asserts abrogation and refutes deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the abrogation of previous laws by Islam is an established fact, supported by the Quran, mutawatir hadiths, and consensus, and how this refutes the claims of those who deny it.

Core Idea
Abrogation is a necessary, rationally permissible fact of divine legislation.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi affirms that Islam has abrogated all previous revelations, a doctrine that is both rationally permissible and actually occurred. He then directly refutes the Jewish and Christian denial of this abrogation, citing decisive evidence from the Quran and the mass-transmitted hadiths. This lesson clarifies the basis for this key belief and its implications for the finality of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation to ensure you grasp the meaning.
Notice the strong language: 'occurred necessarily' (hatm).
2
Identify the two main claims
The passage makes an assertion (abrogation is certain) and then refutes those who deny (Jews, Christians). Identify both parts.
3
Note the evidence provided
Sanusi cites a Quranic verse (Al-Imran 85) and mentions mutawatir hadiths. Understand how these prove abrogation.
Mutawatir hadiths give certain knowledge.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The passage concludes that abrogation is rationally permissible (ja'iz 'aqlan) and actually occurred via revelation (waqi' sam'an) by consensus.
This connects rational possibility with actual occurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونسخه لشرع غيره وقع حتما أذل الله من له منع. ثم أشار إلى الرد على اليهود والنصارى ومن جرى مجراهم، حيث زعموا أن شرع نبينا لم ينسخ شرع أحد من الأنبياء، بقوله: (ونسخه) الله أي: شرع نبينا محمد (لشرع) كل نبي (غيره) صلى الله عليه وسلم (وقع حتما) أي: متحتما لا يقبل التأويل؛ لقوله تعالى: {وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا} [آل عمران: 85] الآية. والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة بلغت جملتها مبلغ التواتر، ومراده رحمه الله تعالى: أن النسخ جائز عقلا واقع سمعا، بإجماع المسلمين.
And its abrogation of the law of others occurred necessarily; Allah has humiliated those who deny it. Then he pointed to the refutation of the Jews and Christians and those who follow their path, since they claimed that the law of our Prophet did not abrogate the law of any of the prophets, by his saying: 'And its abrogation' i.e., the law of our Prophet Muhammad, 'of the law' of every prophet 'other than him' صلى الله عليه وسلم, 'occurred necessarily' i.e., absolutely necessitated, not admitting interpretation; because of His saying تعالى: {And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him} the verse. And the hadiths on this are many, reaching the level of tawātur. And his intent, may Allah have mercy on him, is that abrogation is rationally permissible and actually occurred via revelation, by consensus of the Muslims.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage asserts that the Shari'ah of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ has abrogated all previous laws, and this is an established fact. The author then refutes the claim of Jews, Christians, and others who deny that the Prophet's law abrogates previous scriptures. He explains that the statement 'Its abrogation of the law of others occurred necessarily' means it is absolutely necessitated and not open to interpretation. The evidence is the Quranic verse (Al-Imran 85) which states that only Islam is accepted, implying the invalidity of all other religions. Furthermore, many hadiths on this topic collectively reach the level of tawātur (mass transmission) and thus provide certain knowledge. The author's intent is to affirm that abrogation is both rationally possible and has actually occurred in revelation, as agreed upon by the consensus of Muslims.

إجماع (ijmā')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation contradicts the perpetual validity of previous scriptures.
Correction: Abrogation does not invalidate earlier scriptures for their time; it establishes that Islam is the final and complete revelation for all humanity.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The abrogation of previous laws by Islam is a rationally permissible, divinely ordained fact, proven by the Quran and mutawatir hadiths, and denying it is refuted by Islamic consensus.

The Types of Abrogation: Quran by Quran, Sunnah by Sunnah, Sunnah by Quran
Sanusi enumerates the types of naskh: Quran by Quran, Sunnah by Sunnah, Sunnah by Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of abrogation (naskh) recognized by Sunni scholars: abrogation of the Quran by the Quran, the Sunnah by the Sunnah, and the Sunnah by the Quran, along with examples from the primary sources.

Core Idea
Abrogation in Islamic law operates within the same type or from Sunnah to Quran, never from Quran to Sunnah.

Sanusi, in his commentary on the Jawharat al-Tawhid, outlines the permissible types of abrogation. He clarifies that abrogation only applies to rulings, not to the essential nature of revelation, and gives concrete examples from the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson unpacks each type with its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the text, then read the English translation carefully.
Pay attention to the examples given.
2
Identify the three types
The commentary lists three types. Note the specific examples and the rationale behind each.
The first type involves two Quranic verses; the second involves a hadith; the third involves a change of qibla.
3
Understand the key principle
Notice the condition that abrogation does not imply deficiency in the Prophet. This is a key theological safeguard.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can distinguish the types.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات
عليا
نسخ بعض أحكام شرع نبينا محمد هلا بالبعض ولو قُرآنيَّةٌ ـ مِن نَقص يقتضي محمَّدٍ امتناعه .
[أنواع النسخ ]
وشَمِل البعض في النَّظم ناسخا كان أو منسوخا نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب كحكم والذين يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةً لأَزواجهم بحكم : ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا . لتأخرها نزولا وإن تقدَّمتْ تِلاوةً، ونَسخَ السُّنَّة بالسُّنَّة كحديث : كُنتُ نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور فَزوروها والسُّنَّةِ بالكتاب كحُكم استقبالِ بيت المقدس الثابت بالسُّنَّة الفعلية باستقبالِ الكعبة الثَّابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَوَلِ وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ .
Section of Prophethood. On high. Abrogation of some rulings of the law of our Prophet Muhammad, but not to the extent that necessitates the impossibility of Muhammad. [Types of Abrogation] It included some in the arrangement, whether abrogating or abrogated: abrogation of the Book by the Book, like the ruling 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives' by the ruling 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait for four months and ten days' because it was later in revelation even if earlier in recitation; and abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah, like the hadith 'I forbade you from visiting graves, so visit them'; and the Sunnah by the Book, like the ruling of facing Jerusalem established by the practical Sunnah by facing the Kaaba established by His statement 'So turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram'.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of abrogation as presented in the poem and then lists three types. It begins with the line from the poem stating that abrogation applies to some rulings of the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad, not all, and it does not imply any deficiency in the Prophet. Then the commentary opens the section on 'Types of Abrogation' (أنواع النسخ). It explains that abrogation includes both abrogating and abrogated rulings within the same category. The first type is abrogation of the Quran by the Quran, illustrated by the verse of bequest (2:240) being abrogated by the verse of waiting period (2:234) despite the latter being recited earlier chronologically. The second type is abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah, citing the hadith about visiting graves. The third type is abrogation of the Sunnah by the Quran, exemplified by the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Kaaba based on the Quranic command. The explanation follows the author's order, clarifying each type with concrete examples.

ناسخ
منسوخ

السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That abrogation implies a change in God's knowledge or a deficiency in the Prophet.
Correction: The passage specifies that abrogation only occurs in rulings, not in the essential nature of revelation, and it does not imply any deficiency.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The three permissible types of abrogation are Quran by Quran, Sunnah by Sunnah, and Sunnah by Quran, each supported by explicit examples from revelation.

Theoretical Permissibility of Abrogating Quran by Sunnah
Sanusi affirms theoretical permissibility of abrogating Quran by ahad hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the correct scholarly view permits abrogation of the Quran by even a solitary (ahad) hadith, contrary to those who forbid it.

Core Idea
Even a single authentic hadith can abrogate a Quranic verse.

Sanusi opens by stating the ruling on abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah. He affirms that, according to the majority of scholars, even a solitary (ahad) hadith can abrogate a Quranic verse, despite the objection of some. He then provides the classic example of the bequest verse being abrogated by the prophetic hadith 'No bequest for an heir.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the ruling
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice that Sanusi begins with a clear ruling: the Book can be abrogated by the Sunnah, even if a solitary report. This is the 'correct view.'
2
Understand the opposing opinion
Sanusi mentions that there is a contrary opinion that forbids abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah altogether. Recall that some scholars held this view to protect the Quran's primacy.
3
Analyze the example
The example given is the Quranic command to make bequests for parents and relatives (2:180) being abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest for an heir.' See how the hadith limits the general command.
This hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning, but the example illustrates the principle.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Ask yourself: Why would some scholars reject this? How does this affect our understanding of the relationship between Quran and Sunnah?
The next lesson will add a historical nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكتاب بالسُّنَّة ولو آحادا على الصحيح، خلافا لمن منعه؛ كجواز الوصية للوالدين والأقربين الدال عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ﴾ بحديث: لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثٍ والحقُّ أَنَّه لم يقع إلَّا بالسُّنَّة المتواترة.
And [abrogation of] the Book by the Sunnah, even a solitary [hadith], according to the correct view, contrary to those who forbid it; like the permissibility of bequest for parents and relatives indicated by His statement: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, a bequest for parents and relatives' by the hadith: 'No bequest for an heir.' And the truth is that it only occurred with the mutawatir Sunnah.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage focuses on the fourth type of abrogation: abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah. It states that according to the correct scholarly opinion, even a solitary (ahad) hadith can abrogate the Quran, contra those who forbid this. The example given is the Quranic verse commanding bequests for parents and relatives (2:180) being abrogated by the prophetic hadith 'No bequest for an heir.' However, the passage then qualifies this by stating that as a matter of historical fact, abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah only occurred through mutawatir (massively transmitted) reports, not through solitary hadiths. This distinction reconciles the theoretical permissibility with actual occurrence.

Key Terms
آحاد
الوصية
الوارث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran cannot be abrogated by any hadith; only Quran can abrogate Quran.
Correction: The correct view is that the Sunnah, even if solitary, can abrogate the Quran, as demonstrated by the example of bequests.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the correct view regarding abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah?
A) It is not permitted at all
B) It is permitted only by mutawatir Sunnah
C) It is permitted even by a solitary (ahad) hadith
D) It is permitted only by the Quran itself

Key Takeaway
The correct scholarly view permits abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah, even if the Sunnah is transmitted through a single chain (ahad).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the example: a clear Quranic command to leave bequests for parents and relatives was abrogated by a single hadith. When a prophetic instruction contradicts your natural inclinations or what seems fair, do you submit immediately, or do you rationalize to avoid obedience? What is one area of your life where you have resisted a sunnah because it felt too restrictive?
?
Sanusi states that even an ahad hadith can abrogate a Quranic verse. How deeply do you trust the Sunnah as a source of divine guidance? Is there a prophetic teaching you have dismissed because its chain seemed weak or its ruling difficult? Ask yourself: would you be willing to change a deeply ingrained habit if you discovered it contradicted an authentic hadith, even if it meant discomfort?
?
The minority opinion that forbids abrogation by ahad hadith seems cautious, but the majority allows it. In your own life, do you tend to play it safe with your religion, avoiding anything that seems uncertain? Or do you embrace the full authority of revelation, even when it demands a leap of faith? What is the one area where you are most afraid to let go of your own reasoning and fully trust the Prophet's words?

Historical Actualty: Only Mutawatir Sunnah Abrogated the Quran
Sanusi specifies the historical reality that abrogation only happened via mutawatir Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that although theoretical permissibility extends to ahad hadiths, as a matter of historical fact, abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah occurred only through mutawatir reports.

Core Idea
Historical fact: Only mutawatir Sunnah abrogated the Quran.

After stating the theoretical permissibility, Sanusi adds an important historical qualification. He says that, in reality, abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah never occurred through solitary hadiths; it only happened through mutawatir (massively transmitted) reports. This nuance reconciles the theoretical openness with the actual recorded practice of the companions and early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the sentence carefully
Read the Arabic: 'والحقُّ أَنَّه لم يقع إلَّا بالسُّنَّة المتواترة.' This is a separate statement that modifies the previous ruling.
2
Understand the term 'mutawatir'
Mutawatir means a report transmitted by such a large number of narrators that collusion on a falsehood is impossible. This ensures certainty.
In contrast, ahad hadiths provide probable knowledge.
3
Compare with the previous lesson
The previous lesson said it is theoretically permissible for ahad to abrogate. Here Sanusi says historically it never happened. This is not a contradiction but a distinction between permissibility and occurrence.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
Why would Allah only allow abrogation through certain reports? Perhaps to preserve the Quran's authority while allowing flexibility. Consider the implications for usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكتاب بالسُّنَّة ولو آحادا على الصحيح، خلافا لمن منعه؛ كجواز الوصية للوالدين والأقربين الدال عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ﴾ بحديث: لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثٍ والحقُّ أَنَّه لم يقع إلَّا بالسُّنَّة المتواترة.
And [abrogation of] the Book by the Sunnah, even a solitary [hadith], according to the correct view, contrary to those who forbid it; like the permissibility of bequest for parents and relatives indicated by His statement: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, a bequest for parents and relatives' by the hadith: 'No bequest for an heir.' And the truth is that it only occurred with the mutawatir Sunnah.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage focuses on the fourth type of abrogation: abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah. It states that according to the correct scholarly opinion, even a solitary (ahad) hadith can abrogate the Quran, contra those who forbid this. The example given is the Quranic verse commanding bequests for parents and relatives (2:180) being abrogated by the prophetic hadith 'No bequest for an heir.' However, the passage then qualifies this by stating that as a matter of historical fact, abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah only occurred through mutawatir (massively transmitted) reports, not through solitary hadiths. This distinction reconciles the theoretical permissibility with actual occurrence.

Key Terms
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because ahad hadiths can theoretically abrogate, many instances of abrogation exist from ahad reports.
Correction: Historically, no such abrogation occurred; only mutawatir reports were used.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say is the historical fact about abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah?
A) It occurred with both mutawatir and ahad reports
B) It occurred only with mutawatir reports
C) It never occurred at all
D) It occurred only with ahad reports

Key Takeaway
While ahad hadiths can theoretically abrogate the Quran, historically only mutawatir Sunnah carried out such abrogation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever feel that some of its commands are difficult to follow? This lesson shows that even when a ruling was changed, it was only done through the most certain reports. How does that reality challenge any tendency you might have to dismiss a clear Quranic command based on a weak argument? What commitment can you make today to hold the Quran's rulings as binding until proven otherwise by overwhelming evidence?
?
Imagine you are faced with a situation where a hadith seems to contradict a Quran verse you cherish. How does knowing that only mutawatir reports actually abrogated the Quran affect your reaction? Will you now be more careful to verify the authenticity and strength of the hadith before acting? Answer honestly: have you ever acted on a weak hadith that contradicted a Quranic principle? What will you do differently from now on?

The Three Categories of Naskh
Sanusi classifies abrogated texts into three categories based on what is abrogated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of abrogation in Islamic law: abrogation of both recitation and ruling, recitation only, and ruling only, along with examples from the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Abrogation can affect recitation, ruling, or both — not always the entire text.

Sanusi presents a detailed classification of abrogated texts, showing that abrogation is not limited to removing the entire verse. Sometimes only the recitation is removed while the ruling remains, and sometimes only the ruling is removed while the recitation stays. This lesson breaks down each category with clear examples.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification
Sanusi divides abrogated texts into three categories based on what is abrogated. Read the passage to see the full classification.
2
First category: both abrogated
Examine the example of the verse about ten sucklings that was abrogated in both its recitation and ruling.
3
Second category: recitation abrogated, ruling remains
Examine the example of the stoning verse that was removed from the Quran but the ruling of stoning continued.
4
Third category: ruling abrogated, recitation remains
Examine the example of the bequest verse that was abrogated in ruling but remains in the Quran. Also note the commentary on permissibility.
5
Reflect on the pattern
Consider how each category shows a different aspect of naskh and why this classification is important for understanding Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما شَمِل أيضا ما نُسخت تلاوته وحكمه جميعاً نحو: «عشر رضعات مُحرّماتٍ كان ممَّا يتلى فنُسخن بخمس معلومات. وما نُسخت تلاوته دون حكمه نحو: «الشيخ والشيخة إذا زَنَيا فارجُموهما البَّة نَكالا من الله والله عزيز حكيم كانَ ممَّا يُتلى فَرجَمَ النَّبِيُّ المحصنين . وما نُسخ حكمه دون تلاوته كآية هو والذين يتوفون منكم وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةً لِأَزْوَاجِهِم ﴾ نُسخ بأربعة أشهر وعشرا . فلعل مراده بالجواز عدم الحرمة، لأنه كان في صدر الإسلام عدم حرمة التنفيذ للوصية بالنسبة للوالدين وإن لم يُجز بقية الورثة كالزوج ، والآن يحرم التنفيذ إن لم يجز بقية الورثة كالزوج ، فالوصية الآن صحيحة متوقف تنفيذها على إجازة بقية الورثة.
It also includes that whose recitation and ruling are both abrogated, like: 'Ten sucklings are prohibitions' was among what was recited, then abrogated by five known ones. And that whose recitation is abrogated but not its ruling, like: 'The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, stone them both as a deterrent from Allah, and Allah is Mighty, Wise' was among what was recited, then the Prophet stoned the married ones. And that whose ruling is abrogated but not its recitation, like the verse 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives' was abrogated by four months and ten. Perhaps his intention by 'permissibility' is the absence of prohibition, because in early Islam there was no prohibition of executing the bequest for parents even if the other heirs like the husband did not permit it, but now execution is forbidden if the other heirs do not permit it; thus the bequest is now valid but its execution depends on the permission of the other heirs.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage enumerates three categories of abrogated texts. First, abrogation of both the recitation (tilawah) and the ruling (hukm) — exemplified by the verse about ten sucklings making marriage unlawful, which was originally recited but then abrogated by the verse specifying five sucklings. Second, abrogation of the recitation only while the ruling remains — exemplified by the verse prescribing stoning for married adulterers, which was removed from the Quranic text but the ruling of stoning continued to be applied by the Prophet. Third, abrogation of the ruling only while the recitation remains — exemplified by the verse about bequest for wives being abrogated by the verse establishing a waiting period of four months and ten days. The passage then comments on the previous example of bequest for parents and relatives, clarifying that the permissibility (jawaz) refers to the absence of prohibition (hurmah) in early Islam, but now the bequest is valid only if the other heirs permit it.

Key Terms
تلاوة
حكم
رضعات
رجم
وصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That abrogation means the entire text is lost.
Correction: This passage shows that sometimes only the ruling or only the recitation is abrogated.

Checkpoint
Which example is given for abrogation of the recitation only (نسخت تلاوته دون حكمه)?
A) Ten sucklings
B) Stoning of the married adulterer
C) Bequest for wives
D) Bequest for parents

Key Takeaway
Abrogation can remove the recitation, the ruling, or both, and it is important to distinguish between the textual existence of a verse and its legal applicability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse in the Quran, do you automatically assume it is still legally binding? How will you now investigate whether its ruling has been abrogated, and what does that require of you as a student of knowledge?
?
The passage mentions that the stoning verse was abrogated in recitation but its ruling remained. Are you willing to accept a ruling that is not explicitly in the Quran today? What does that mean for your understanding of prophetic authority?
?
If you have ever ignored a verse because its ruling was abrogated, consider: does its continued recitation still have a purpose? How can you incorporate such verses into your daily recitation and reflection despite their legal inapplicability?

Abrogation (Naskh) and Its Two Types
Commentator defines two types of naskh with Quranic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of abrogation (naskh) and the significance of al-Shafi‘i's view that naskh without substitute did not occur.

Core Idea
Abrogation can occur with or without a substitute, but the latter type is only theoretical.

The concept of abrogation (naskh) is central to understanding how divine rulings interact over time. The commentator here clarifies two distinct types of naskh: one that brings a substitute ruling and one that does not. This distinction is illustrated with specific Quranic verses and concludes with an important methodological point from Imam al-Shafi‘i.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the two types being defined.
The passage includes a section heading and footnote markers.
2
Identify the two categories
Look for the two types: naskh to a substitute (badal) and naskh without a substitute (ghayr badal). Find their Quranic examples.
The first example refers to two verses in Surah al-Anfal.
3
Understand al-Shafi‘i's position
Note that Imam al-Shafi‘i held that naskh without a substitute did not actually occur. The verse from Surah al-Mujadila is interpreted as having a substitute: absolute permissibility.
This reflects a scholarly debate about the reality of naskh without substitute.
4
Reflect on 'jawaz mutlaq'
The substitute in the verse is defined as absolute permissibility (jawaz mutlaq), which includes permission (ibaha) and recommendation (istihbab). Consider how this applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات
والنَّسخ إلى بدل كما في آيتي الأنفال (۱)، وإلى غير بدل كقوله تعالى: يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا نَجَيْتُمُ الرَّسُولَ ﴾ [المجادلة: (۱۲] الآية، فإنَّ وجوب تقديم الصَّدقةِ (۲) على مناجاته ، نسخ بلا بدل ، والحقُّ أنَّ هذا القسم لم يقع نُسْخَ (۳) وفاقا للشَّافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه، والبدل في هذه الآية: الجَوازُ المُطلَقُ الصَّادِق بالإباحة والاستحباب.
Section on prophethoods. And abrogation to a substitute, as in the two verses of al-Anfal (1), and to a non-substitute, like His statement: 'O you who have believed, when you [wish to] consult the Messenger...' [al-Mujadila: 12], for the obligation of giving charity (2) before his consultation was abrogated without a substitute. And the truth is that this type did not occur (3) according to al-Shafi‘i, may God be pleased with him. And the substitute in this verse is the absolute permissibility which applies to permission and recommendation.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage defines two types of abrogation (naskh) in Islamic law, illustrated by Quranic verses. It states: naskh to a substitute, as in the two verses of Surah al-Anfal (which deal with the number of fighters), and naskh without a substitute, as in the verse of Surah al-Mujadila where the obligation of giving charity before private consultation was abrogated entirely. The commentator then asserts that according to al-Shafi‘i, the second type (without substitute) did not actually occur, and the substitute in the verse is the general permissibility (jawaz mutlaq) which includes both permission (ibaha) and recommendation (istihbab).

Key Terms

بدل
جواز مطلق
إباحة
استحباب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation always requires a substitute ruling.
Correction: Abrogation can be without a substitute in theory, but according to al-Shafi‘i, it did not occur in the Quran. The example of the charity verse is interpreted as having a substitute of absolute permissibility.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of al-Shafi‘i regarding the type of abrogation without a substitute?
A) It is the most common type.
B) It did not actually occur.
C) It is permissible only for the Prophet.
D) It requires a substitute in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Abrogation (naskh) occurs either with a substitute ruling or without, but al-Shafi‘i holds that the latter never actually occurred, making the distinction largely theoretical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn that some abrogated rulings are replaced only by a general permissibility, does that challenge your assumption that every abrogated ruling must have a clear substitute? How does this make you rethink the wisdom behind abrogation?
?

?
Do you trust the scholarly consensus (like al-Shafi‘i's assertion) that abrogation without substitute never actually occurred, even though the Quranic example appears to be one? How does that affect your confidence in your own understanding of revelation?

Believing in Aisha's Innocence from the Slander
The commentator defines the obligation to believe in Aisha's innocence and recounts the slander incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that affirming Aisha's innocence from the slander is a legally obligatory belief supported by the Quran, consensus, and authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Believing in Aisha's innocence is a mandatory article of faith.

The slander against Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) was a grave event in early Islam. This lesson establishes why every Muslim must believe in her innocence and presents the primary evidences from revelation and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the phrase 'يجب شرعاً' which indicates a legal obligation.
This passage uses both explicit ruling and a historical narrative.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that every legally responsible person must believe in Aisha's innocence. This is the main doctrinal point.
3
Examine the evidence provided
The commentator mentions three types of evidence: the Quran (ten verses from Surat al-Nur), the consensus of the Ummah, and authentic hadiths. List them.
This shows that the obligation is well-established.
4
Understand the historical context
Read the narrative about the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq. This clarifies why the accusation arose and how the Quran vindicated Aisha.
Knowing the story reinforces the seriousness.
5
Reflect on the gravity
Realize that doubting or denying Aisha's innocence contradicts clear Quranic verses and consensus, making it a grave matter.
The common misunderstanding is that it's a minor issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات
(وبَر أَنْ) يعني : أنَّه يجب شرعاً على كلِّ مكلَّف أنْ يعتقد براءةَ أمّ المؤمنين (لِعَائِشَة) بنت أبي بكر الصديق (مِمَّا رَمَوْا)، أي: من الإفك الذي رَمَاها به المُنافقونَ وقَدْفُوها به ، وكانَ الذي تولى كبره عبد الله بن أُبي بن سلول لعنه الله ، كما جاءَ به القرآنُ وانعقد عليه إجماع الأمة، ووردَتْ به الأحاديثُ الصَّحيحة ؛ حين كانتْ في غزوة بني المصطلق ، تخلّفتْ في طَلب عِقْدِها ، وكانَ مِن جَزْع أظفار ، فَحُمِل هَوْدَجُها ظنَّا أَنَّها فيه ، وسَارَ القومُ ورجعت فلم تجدهم ، فمرَّ بها صفوان بن المُعطّل ، فحملها ولم ينظر إليها وقاد بها البعير موليها ظهره ، حتّى أدرك بها النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فرموها به ، فأنزل الله تعالى فى براءتها عشر آيات من أول سورة النُّور .
The section on prophethood. (And it is necessary that) means: it is legally obligatory upon every legally responsible person to believe in the innocence of the Mother of the Believers Aisha bint Abi Bakr al-Siddiq from what they accused her of, i.e., from the slander which the hypocrites accused her of and slandered her with. And the one who took the lead in it was Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul, may Allah curse him. As it came in the Quran and the consensus of the Ummah is established upon it, and authentic hadiths were reported concerning it. It was during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq; she lagged behind seeking her necklace, and it was made from Yemeni beads, so her camel litter was carried thinking she was in it, and the people departed. She returned and did not find them. Then Safwan ibn al-Mu'attal passed by her, so he made his camel kneel for her to ride, and she rode, and he led the camel with his back turned to her until he caught up with the Prophet (peace be upon him) with her. Then they (the hypocrites) accused her with it. So Allah the Exalted revealed ten verses from the beginning of Surat al-Nur concerning her innocence.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof passage. It first states the obligation: every legally responsible person must believe in Aisha's innocence from the slander (ifk) thrown by hypocrites. It identifies the chief slanderer as Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul. Then it provides the evidence: the Quran (ten verses from Surat al-Nur), consensus of the Ummah, and authentic hadiths. It then narrates the incident from the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq to clarify the context: Aisha lagged behind looking for her necklace, her empty litter was carried off, she was found by Safwan ibn al-Mu'attal who brought her to the Prophet, and the hypocrites accused her. The passage establishes that denying or doubting her innocence is a grave matter.

الإفك
أم المؤمنين
إجماع الأمة

Misconception: Doubting Aisha's innocence is a minor sin.
Correction: The text implies that denying or doubting her innocence is a grave matter that contradicts Quranic revelation and consensus, and can amount to disbelief.

Key Takeaway
Believing in Aisha's innocence from the slander is a mandatory belief supported by Quran, consensus, and authentic hadith.

The Obligation to Believe in the Superiority of the Companions and the First Three Generations
The commentator enumerates the obligation and proofs of the Companions' superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the superiority of the Prophet's Companions and the Followers, and the proofs for their rank.

Core Idea
The Companions are the best generation after the prophets, with varying degrees of honor.

This lesson addresses a foundational belief in Sunni Islam: the superiority of the Companions and the early generations. The commentator explains why this is obligatory to believe, citing Quran and hadith. Pay attention to the distinction between the general honor of companionship and the higher rank of those who fought and sacrificed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic heading and verse 75, then the translation. Notice the emphasis on 'his Companions' and the phrase 'best of generations'.
2
Identify the three groups mentioned
The passage mentions the Prophet's generation (Companions), then the Followers, and then those who follow the Followers. Understand the scope of each group.
The heading uses 'قرنه وأصحابه ثم التابعين' but the commentary focuses on the Companions.
3
Understand the proofs for superiority
The commentator cites Quranic verses and a hadith. Note that the Companions are superior to all non-prophets before and after them. Also grasp the nuance that there are degrees among them.
The hadith 'Allah chose my Companions over the worlds except prophets' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب اعتقاد خيرية قرنه وأصحابه ثم التابعين
٧٥ - وصَحْبُهُ صَحْبُهُ خيرُ القُرُونِ فَاسْتَمِعْ فَتَابِعِي فتابعٌ لِمَنْ تَبِعْ
ثمَّ أشار إلى حكم واجب الاعتقاد أيضاً بقوله (وَصَحْبُهُ) صلى الله عليه وسلم ، أي: كل فردٍ مِن الصَّحابة الذين آمنوا به وصَحِبُوه ولو قليلا ، والمراد من كان صحابيا في نفس الأمر، وَصلَ إلينا عِلْمُ صُحبَتِه أم لا ، (خَيْرُ) أهل (القُرُونِ) المتأخرة، أي: أفضلهم ، وأكثرهم ثواباً ، لأنَّهم آووا ونصروا ، وأما أفضليتهم على القرون المُتقدِّمة غیر الأنبياء فلا كلامَ فيها ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ [الفتح: ۱۸]. ﴿وَالسَّبِقُونَ الْأَوَّلُونَ ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٠]. ولحديث: «إنّ الله اختار أصحابي على العالمين سوى النَّبيِّين والمرسلينَ» ولا يخفى ترجيح رتبة مَن لازمه صلى الله عليه وسلم وقاتل معه أو قتل تحت رايته على مَن لم يُلازمه أو لم يحضر معه مشهداً ، وعلى مَن كلمه يسيرًا أو ماشاه قليلا أو رآه على بُعدٍ أو في حال الطفوليَّة ؛ وإِنْ كانَ شرَفُ الصُّحبةِ حاصلًا للجميع ، وأمَّا أفضل الصَّحابة فيأتي التصريح به في قوله:
The heading: 'Obligation of believing in the goodness of his generation and his Companions, then the Followers.' 
75 - And his Companions, his Companions are the best of generations, so listen, then a follower, then a follower of those who followed. 
Then he pointed to another obligatory ruling of belief by his saying 'and his Companions' (peace be upon him), meaning: every individual among the Companions who believed in him and accompanied him even briefly. And what is meant is whoever was a Companion in reality, whether knowledge of his companionship reached us or not. ('Good') of the people of the later generations, meaning: the best of them and the most rewarded, because they gave shelter and supported. As for their superiority over the earlier generations other than the prophets, there is no debate about it; due to His statement: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers' [al-Fath:18] and 'And the foremost, the first' [al-Tawba:100], and due to the hadith: 'Indeed Allah chose my Companions over the worlds except the prophets and messengers.' And it is not hidden that the rank of one who accompanied him (peace be upon him) and fought with him or was killed under his banner is higher than one who did not accompany him or did not attend a battle with him, and than one who spoke with him briefly or walked with him a little or saw him from a distance or in childhood, even though the honor of companionship is attained for all. As for the best of the Companions, the explicit statement will come in his saying:
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof passage. It begins with a heading: it is obligatory to believe in the superiority of the Prophet's generation (the Companions) and then the Followers. The verse (line 75) states 'his Companions are the best of generations.' The commentary explains that 'his Companions' means every individual Companion regardless of length of companionship. 'Good of the later generations' means they are the best and most rewarded because they gave shelter and support. Their superiority over earlier non-prophet generations is proven by Quranic verses (pleasure of Allah on believers, and the foremost) and a hadith that Allah chose the Companions over all except prophets. The passage then clarifies that there are degrees among Companions: those who accompanied, fought, or were martyred are higher than those with brief or distant interaction, though all share the honor of companionship. The best of the Companions is deferred to a later statement.

Key Terms
الصحابة
خير القرون
التابعون
الشرف الصحبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Companions are of equal rank and status.
Correction: While all Companions share the honor of companionship, the passage explains that those who accompanied the Prophet closely, fought with him, or were martyred have a higher rank than those with brief or distant interaction.

Checkpoint
What is the proof for the superiority of the Companions over later generations other than prophets?
A) Only the Quran verse 'And the foremost, the first'.
B) Consensus of the scholars.
C) The Quranic verses and the hadith that Allah chose the Companions over the worlds except prophets.
D) The hadith alone.

Key Takeaway
The Companions of the Prophet are the best generation after the prophets, and it is obligatory to believe in their superiority, while also acknowledging the varying degrees of their rank based on their service and sacrifice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Companions' rank is based on their sacrifice and support of the Prophet, what does your own support of Islam today look like? Are you willing to give as they gave, even at the cost of comfort or safety?
?
You profess that the Companions are the best generation, but do you truly honor them in your heart, or do you sometimes allow criticism or indifference to creep in? Examine your inner state before Allah.
?
The passage says even a brief companionship grants honor, but the highest rank is for those who fought and accompanied. In your own life, are you content with minimal effort in serving the Prophet's legacy, or are you actively striving for a rank that demands sacrifice?

The Best of the Companions: The Caliphs
Declares the best Companions are the caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the best of the Companions are those who were entrusted with the caliphate, specifically the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

Core Idea
The best Companions are the caliphs, led by Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali.

This lesson focuses on a concise yet powerful statement from the author about the hierarchy among the Companions. It establishes that the highest rank belongs to those who succeeded the Prophet in leading the community, a key tenet of Sunni belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic
Read the short Arabic sentence: 'Qism al-nubuwwat. Wa-khayruhum man wulliya al-khilafah.' Notice the section heading.
The phrase 'Qism al-nubuwwat' signals a new section.
2
Understand the meaning
Translate it: 'And the best of them is the one who was entrusted with the caliphate.' Reflect on who 'them' refers to—the Prophets or the Companions? The context makes it clear: it refers to the Companions.
3
Identify the key point
The author asserts that the best Companions are those who became caliphs. This includes Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali, and this order reflects their virtue.
This is a foundational Sunni belief about the superiority of the four caliphs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات
وخيرهم مَن وُلِّيَ الخلافة
والقَرْن: أهل زمانٍ واحدٍ مُتقارب، اشتركوا في أمرٍ من الأمور المقصودة. وسُمِّي قرنا : لأنَّه يَقْرِنُ أُمَّةً بأُمَّةٍ وعالما بعالم ، ثم جُعل اسما للوقت أو لأهله ، فقرنه الا الله مُدَّة أصحابه من البعث إلى آخر من مات منهم ، وهي مائة وعشرون سنة ، أو نفس أصحابه ، وقرن التابعينَ: مِن سنة مائة إلى نحو سبعين ، وقرن أتباع التابعين : تمَّ إلى حدود العشرين ومائتين، والله أعلم
وقوله: (فَاسْتَمِعْ) ، تكملةٌ
Section of prophethoods. And the best of them is the one who was entrusted with the caliphate. And al-qarn (the generation): people of one close time period, who share in some of the intended matters. And it was called a 'qarn' because it connects a nation to a nation and a world to a world. Then it was made a name for the time or its people. So the qarn of the Companions of Allah is the duration of his Companions from the mission to the last of them who died, which is one hundred and twenty years, or it is the Companions themselves. And the qarn of the Followers: from year one hundred to about seventy. And the qarn of the Followers of the Followers: completed to about the two hundred and twenties. And Allah knows best. And His saying: 'So listen' is a completion.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is both a doctrinal statement and a lexical definition. It begins by stating that the best of the Companions is the one who was given the caliphate, referring to the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Then it defines the term 'qarn' (generation) as a group of people from a close time period who share common characteristics. The reason it is called 'qarn' is because it connects one nation and world to another. Over time, it became used for either the time period or the people of that time. It then specifies the durations: the generation of the Companions spans from the Prophet's mission until the death of the last Companion, about 120 years. Alternatively, it may refer to the Companions themselves. The generation of the Followers is from around year 100 AH to about 170 AH, and the generation of the Followers of the Followers extends to around 220 AH. The passage ends with a note that the word 'fastami' in the poem is a completion.

Key Terms
خلافة (caliphate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only Abu Bakr is the best Companion, and others are less.
Correction: The passage states 'the one who was entrusted with the caliphate' collectively, referring to all four caliphs, not just one.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who are the best of the Companions?
A) All the Companions equally
B) Those who were given the caliphate
C) The ones who migrated first
D) The ones who fought in Badr

Key Takeaway
The best of the Companions are those who held the caliphate, namely the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The text says that the best Companions are those who held the caliphate. Have you ever reflected on the tremendous responsibility these four individuals bore? What trust has Allah placed in your hands today—whether in your family, work, or community—and are you upholding it with the same dedication and sincerity as those caliphs?
?
The caliphs were entrusted with leadership over the entire ummah. But before that, each of them was tested in smaller trusts. Think of a small trust you have neglected recently (a promise, a duty, a secret). What specific step can you take today to repair that breach and become more trustworthy?
?
Do you truly love the Companions, especially the caliphs, as the Prophet commanded? If your heart feels any indifference or even a whisper of doubt about their excellence, what is the root of that? Ask Allah to purify your heart and to fill it with love for those He has honored.

Defining the Generation (Qarn) and Its Durations
Defines qarn and gives durations of early generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of qarn (generation) and the specific years associated with the first three generations of Muslims.

Core Idea
A generation is defined by shared characteristics and time, not a fixed number of years.

This lesson unpacks the author's technical definition of 'qarn' (generation), a term often misunderstood as simply 100 years. The passage provides both the linguistic rationale and the precise timelines for the Companions, Followers, and Followers of the Followers.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of qarn
Start with the passage: 'Wal-qarn: ahlu zamanin wahidin mutaqarib...' Understand the definition and the reason it is called qarn.
Notice the linguistic root: qarn from qarana (to join).
2
Examine the three generations
The passage lists three generations: the Companions, the Followers, and the Followers of the Followers. Note the specific years given for each.
The Companions' generation is 120 years, the Followers from 100 AH to about 170 AH, and the next to about 220 AH.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these specific generations and timelines matter. They highlight the continuity and transmission of knowledge from the Prophet's era onward.
This is important for understanding the chain of narration in hadith.

Source Text

Section of prophethoods. And the best of them is the one who was entrusted with the caliphate. And al-qarn (the generation): people of one close time period, who share in some of the intended matters. And it was called a 'qarn' because it connects a nation to a nation and a world to a world. Then it was made a name for the time or its people. So the qarn of the Companions of Allah is the duration of his Companions from the mission to the last of them who died, which is one hundred and twenty years, or it is the Companions themselves. It begins by stating that the best of the Companions is the one who was given the caliphate, referring to the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Then it defines the term 'qarn' (generation) as a group of people from a close time period who share common characteristics. Correction: The passage defines qarn by shared characteristics and gives specific durations that are not necessarily 100 years, e.g., the Companions are 120 years.

A) 100 years

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions' generation lasted 120 years. Do you see them as distant historical figures or as living examples whose teachings are immediately relevant to your life? What specific action will you take today to draw closer to their legacy?
?
The Followers lived from 100 AH to 170 AH—closer to our time. Does knowing the precise lengths of these generations make you feel part of an unbroken chain? What are you doing to strengthen your link in that chain for the generations after you?
?
The text defines a generation by shared characteristics, not just time. What shared characteristics of faith and practice do you have with the early Muslims? Name one quality they possessed that you lack, and commit to a concrete step to develop it this week.

Definition of the Tabi'i (Follower) and Conditions
Defines a Tabi'i and discusses conditions for being considered a Follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a Tabi'i and the conditions required for someone to be considered a Follower, as well as the differing scholarly views on the necessity of companionship.

Core Idea
A Tabi'i is defined by meeting a Companion who met the Prophet, with conditions on life and faith.

This lesson establishes the definition of the Tabi'i, the second generation of Muslims after the Companions. The source passage presents the primary definition and a differing view, highlighting the importance of meeting conditions. Understanding these distinctions helps in evaluating hadith narrations and recognizing the status of the Followers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice that the passage ends abruptly, possibly indicating a continuation.
2
Identify the two definitions of Tabi'i
The passage presents a primary definition and then a second opinion. Identify the key elements of each: the first requires meeting a Companion who met the Prophet, both alive and believing, in a normal meeting; the second adds the condition of companionship.
Also note that 'discernment' (tamyiz) is not required for a Tabi'i.
3
Reflect on the conditions and their implications
Consider why these conditions matter for the classification of narrators and the transmission of hadith. How does the definition affect the reliability of a Tabi'i as a narrator?
The condition of 'normal meeting' excludes extraordinary meetings like meeting a dead Companion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَتَابِعِيْ يعني أَنَّ رُتبتَهم تَلِي رتبة الصَّحابة مِن غير تراخ كبير. والتّابعيُّ: مَن لَقي الصَّحابي الَّذِي لَقِيه صلى الله عليه وسلم ، حيًّا مؤمنًا حيَّا مؤمنا به، لقيا على غير وجه حرق العادة. وقيل: لا يكفي مجرَّد اللقاء ، بل لا بُدَّ مِن الصحبة لمزيَّة لقائه على لقاء غيره من صلحاء أمَّتِه ، ولا يشترط فيه التمييز ، ولو شُرِط في الصَّحابي
Then the Followers: meaning that their rank follows the rank of the Companions without great delay. And the Tabi'i (Follower) is: one who met the Companion who met him (peace be upon him), alive and believing, alive and believing in him, a meeting not in an extraordinary manner. And it is said: mere meeting is not sufficient, rather companionship is necessary due to the superiority of his meeting over meeting others among the righteous of his community. And discernment (tamyiz) is not required of him, even if it is required of the Companion.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Tabi'i' (Follower), the second generation of Muslims after the Companions. It first explains that the rank of the Followers follows that of the Companions without a long gap. Then it defines a Tabi'i as one who met a Companion who himself met the Prophet, while both were alive and believing, in a normal (non-miraculous) meeting. It then presents a differing view that mere meeting is not enough; rather, there must be some form of companionship to distinguish his meeting from that of other righteous people. Finally, it states that discernment (tamyiz, i.e., the ability to distinguish) is not required for a Tabi'i, even if it is required for a Companion (which is discussed elsewhere). The passage is cut off before completing the comparison.

Key Terms
تابعي (Tabi'i/Follower)
صحابي (Companion)
لقيا (meeting)
تمييز (discernment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply meeting any Companion automatically qualifies one as a Tabi'i.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Companion met must have met the Prophet, both must be alive and believing, and the meeting must be normal. Additionally, some scholars require actual companionship beyond just meeting.

Checkpoint
What is the minimum condition for being a Tabi'i according to the first definition?
A) To have accompanied a Companion for a long time
B) To have met a Companion who met the Prophet, both alive and believing
C) To have seen the Prophet
D) To be a righteous Muslim

Key Takeaway
A Tabi'i is primarily defined as one who met a Companion who met the Prophet, alive and believing, in a normal meeting, with differing views on the necessity of companionship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly grateful for the chain of Companions and Followers who transmitted the faith to you? What is one concrete way you can honor their sacrifice in your daily life starting today?
?
The lesson distinguishes between mere 'meeting' and 'companionship' with the Prophet's legacy. Do you merely 'meet' the Quran and Sunnah in passing, or do you develop companionship with them? What would change if you sought deeper companionship this week?
?
You are alive and believing right now, just like the Followers were when they met the Companions. But are you spiritually alive? If your faith feels stagnant, what one step will you take before tonight to revive it?
