Obligation of Belief in Recording Angels
Obligation of belief and distinction of good and evil deeds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the recording angels is obligatory and that good and evil deeds are recorded distinctly, as indicated by transmitted traditions.

Core Idea
Every deed is recorded distinctly, and the record of a believer begins with sins that are forgiven.

This lesson begins by affirming the obligation of belief in the guardian angels who record deeds. The author then cites traditions showing that good deeds are written separately from evil ones, and he reports a specific saying about how the records of believers and disbelievers are presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice the opening statement of obligation.
2
Identify the distinction
Look for how good deeds and evil deeds are written separately. What is said about the believer's book and the disbeliever's book?
The believer's sins are at the beginning and then forgiven; the disbeliever's good deeds are at the beginning and then rejected.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this distinction matters. The author is emphasizing that the recording is just and detailed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة

وظواهر الآثارِ أنَّ الحسنات تُكتَبُ مُتميّزة عن السيئات؛ فقيل: إِنَّ سيِّئات المؤمن أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه ذنوبُكَ قد سَتَرتُها وغفرتُها. وحسنات الكافر أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه حسناتك قد رددتها عليك وما قبلتها.

ولو ذهل حال صدور ذلك الفعل عنه؛ لأنَّه ليس الغرض من الكتب الإثابة ولا المعاقبة؛ ففي حديث ابن عباس في قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ﴾ [ق: ۱۸]، قال: يُكتب كل ما يتكلّم به من خير أو شرّ؛ حتَّى أنَّه ليُكتب قوله: أكلت شربت، ذهبت، جئت، رأيت، حتَّى إذا كان يوم الخميس عُرِضَ قوله وعمله؛ فَأَقِرَّ منه ما كان من خير أو شر، وأُلْغِيَ سَائِرُه.

ثمَّ هذه الكتابة مما يجب الإيمان به، ليست لحاجة دعت إلى ذلك، وإنَّما يَعلم حكمتها سبحانه، على أنَّ فائدتها أنَّ العبد إذا علم بها استحيا، وترك المعصية، وقيل: لأنَّهم شهود بين الله تعالى وبين خلقه، ولذا يقال للعبد يوم القيامة: كفى بنفسك اليوم عليك حسيبا، وبالكرام الكاتبين شهودا.
The obligation of belief in the guardians (al-hafazah) and the scribes of deeds from among the angels. And the apparent meanings of the traditions indicate that good deeds are written distinguished from evil deeds. For it is said: Indeed, the evil deeds of the believer are at the beginning of his book, and at its end: 'These are your sins which I have concealed and forgiven.' And the good deeds of the disbeliever are at the beginning of his book, and at its end: 'These are your good deeds which I have returned to you and not accepted.' And if he forgets at the moment of performing that action, it is because the purpose of writing is neither reward nor punishment. For in the hadith of Ibn Abbas concerning the saying of Allah Most High: 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), he said: 'Everything that one speaks of good or evil is written, even to the point that his words are written: I ate, I drank, I went, I came, I saw. Then when Thursday comes, his speech and his action are presented, and what was of good or evil is confirmed from it, and the rest is discarded.' Then this writing is one of the things belief in which is obligatory. It is not due to any need that calls for it; rather, He, glorified, knows its wisdom. Among its benefits is that when the servant knows of it, he feels shy and abandons disobedience. And it is said: because they are witnesses between Allah Most High and His creation. Hence it is said to the servant on the Day of Resurrection: 'Sufficient is your own soul this day as a reckoner against you, and the noble scribes as witnesses.'
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation of belief in the recording angels (al-hafazah al-katabah) and explains the nature of their recording of deeds. The author states that the outward indications of the transmitted traditions show that good deeds are written distinctly from evil deeds. He then reports a statement that the believer's evil deeds are placed at the beginning of his book, and at the end it is said that they have been concealed and forgiven, while the disbeliever's good deeds are at the beginning and then returned and not accepted. The author then explains that even if one forgets at the moment of performing an action, the writing still occurs because the purpose is not reward or punishment. He cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas regarding the verse 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), where Ibn Abbas said that every word of good or evil is written, including mundane statements, and then on Thursday the speech and action are presented and only the good or evil is confirmed while the rest is canceled. The author then emphasizes that belief in this writing is obligatory, not because God has any need, but its wisdom includes that the servant, upon knowing that his deeds are recorded, will feel shy and avoid sin. Another benefit mentioned is that the angels serve as witnesses between Allah and His creation, so on the Day of Resurrection it will be said to the servant: 'Sufficient is your own soul as a reckoner against you, and the noble scribes as witnesses.'

Key Terms
الحفظة (al-hafazah)
الكتبة (al-katabah)
الملائكة (angels)
الإيمان (faith)
الآثار (traditions)
السيئات (evil deeds)
الحسنات (good deeds)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that good and evil deeds are recorded in the same list or that the order doesn't matter.
Correction: The passage clarifies that good deeds are written distinctly from evil deeds, and the record of a believer begins with sins that are forgiven, while the disbeliever's record begins with good deeds that are not accepted.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the believer's sins at the end of his book?
A) They are written and left as is
B) They are concealed and forgiven
C) They are returned to him
D) They are discarded

Key Takeaway
Belief in the recording angels is obligatory, and deeds are written distinctly with a just order for believers and disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own book of deeds, do you live with the confidence that your sins—though many—will be forgiven if you are a believer? Or do you treat them lightly, assuming they will be covered without genuine repentance?
?
The disbeliever's good deeds are returned and not accepted because of lack of faith. What does this teach you about the priority of faith over outward actions? In your daily life, are you more concerned with the appearance of your deeds or with the state of your heart before Allah?
?
If the recording angels are writing every deed distinctly at this very moment, what sin or good deed have you committed today that you would be ashamed or proud to see at the beginning of your book? How does this awareness change what you will do in the next hour?

The Comprehensiveness of Deed Recording
Comprehensive recording of deeds, including words, and the weekly presentation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every word and action is recorded, even if the person forgets, and that the purpose is not immediate reward or punishment but a weekly presentation.

Core Idea
Every word is recorded, and on Thursday deeds are presented and only good or evil is retained.

In this lesson, the author addresses the comprehensiveness of recording. He explains that even if a person forgets, the writing still happens because the purpose is not reward or punishment. He then cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas from Surah Qaf, which states that every word is recorded, including mundane statements, and that on Thursday deeds are presented and only the good or evil is kept.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the initial statement about forgetfulness.
2
Understand the hadith
Pay attention to the hadith of Ibn Abbas. What does it say about the recording of words? What happens on Thursday?
Even mundane statements like 'I ate' are recorded, but they are later discarded.
3
Identify the purpose
The author states that the purpose of writing is not reward or punishment. Why then is it done? The hadith implies it is for record and presentation.

Source Text

?

?

?
Imagine your words being presented before Allah this Thursday. If only the good and evil remain, which of your recent words would you be ashamed to have confirmed? What will you do about it before that day comes?

Wisdom and Benefits of Deed Recording
Wisdom and benefits of obligatory belief in recording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind the recording of deeds and the benefits for the servant, including shame and the role of angels as witnesses.

Core Idea
Recording is for the servant's benefit: to inspire shame and provide witnesses.

In this final part of the passage, the author explains why belief in the recording of deeds is obligatory. He states that it is not because Allah needs it, but rather we submit to His wisdom. Among the benefits are that the servant, knowing his deeds are recorded, feels shy and abandons sin. Additionally, the angels serve as witnesses between Allah and His creation, as will be testified on the Day of Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the emphasis on obligation and wisdom.
2
Identify the benefits
List the benefits mentioned: causing shyness and abandoning sin, and the angels as witnesses.
Also note the quote from the Day of Resurrection.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the author emphasizes that Allah does not need this recording. What does that teach us about Allah's independence?

?
Knowing that your every deed is recorded by noble angels, what is one sin you have been committing secretly that you must now abandon out of shame before Allah? Will you make a firm intention to leave it today?
?
The passage says the recording is not due to any need of Allah, but for your benefit. How does this change your attitude towards the angels who write your deeds? Do you live as if they are present with you?
?
On the Day of Judgment, your own soul will testify against you. If your deeds were to be shown to you now, would you be proud or ashamed? What deed do you most regret and how will you rectify it from this moment?

Recording Even Moans in Sickness
Definition, ruling, proof, and linguistic and hadith qualification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even involuntary sounds like moans are recorded, based on the generality of the verse, but with a condition from hadith that links it to prior good deeds.

Core Idea
Every word is recorded, but Allah's mercy spares the distressed servant.

This passage tackles a subtle question: are moans of illness recorded? The author shows that the general verse 'Not a word does he utter...' includes them, but then introduces a hadith that tempers this, interpreting the moan as being recorded only if the person had prior good deeds. This demonstrates how Qur'anic generality can be qualified by prophetic teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall flow. Notice the author defines a term, gives a ruling, then provides a linguistic explanation and a hadith.
2
Focus on the main proof
Identify how the verse 'Not a word does he utter...' is used. The author says the word 'qawl' in a negation context implies generality, so every utterance is recorded.
3
Understand the qualification
The hadith of Anas and Ali show that the moan is recorded only if the person had good deeds before illness; during distress, nothing is written. This resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Reflect on the lesson's nuance
Notice the balance between blanket recording and divine mercy. This passage teaches that divine justice is precise and context-sensitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذهول عن الشيء: نسيانه والغفلة عنه.

يكتبون عليه حتى الأنين الصادر عن طبيعته في المرض كما نُقِل أي: نقله أئمة الدين وعلماء المسلمين وقالوا به، ومن أعظمهم الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه، ومثله لا يُقال بالرأي، تمسكوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ﴾ [ق: ١٨]، إذ وقوع «قول» في سياق النفي يقتضي العموم.

والأنين: مصدر أَنَّ الرجل يئن بالكسر أنينا وأنانا – بالضم - صوت؛ فالذكر: آن، على فاعل، والأنثى: أنة.

أنه يكتب

وينبغي حمل قوله: حتى الأنين في المرض على معنى له في مرضه خيرات وطاعات؛ لما في حديث أنس، قال: رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا ابتلي الله العبد ببلاء في جسده؛ قال الله للملك: اكتب له صالح عمله الذي كان يعمله؛ فإن شفاه غسله وطهره، وإن قبضه غفر له ورحمه». وفي حديث علي رضي الله عنه رفعه: «يُوحي الله إلى الحفظة: لا تكتبوا على عبدي عند ضجره شيئًا».
And forgetfulness of a thing is its oblivion and heedlessness of it. They write upon him even the moan that proceeds from his nature in sickness, as has been transmitted, meaning: the imams of the religion and the scholars of the Muslims transmitted it and stated it, and among the greatest of them is Imam Malik, may Allah be pleased with him. And the like of it is not said by [personal] opinion. They adhered to the saying of Allah Most High: 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), since the occurrence of 'word' in the context of negation necessitates generality. And 'al-anin' is the verbal noun: a man groans (ya'in) with a kasra, aninan and ananan (with damm) — he makes a sound. So the male is 'ann' on the pattern of fa'il, and the female is 'annah'. That it is written. And it is appropriate to interpret his saying 'even the moan in sickness' as meaning that he has in his sickness good deeds and acts of obedience, because of the hadith of Anas that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'When Allah afflicts a servant with a trial in his body, Allah says to the angel: Write for him the righteous deed which he used to do; for if He heals him, He washes and purifies him, and if He takes him, He forgives him and has mercy on him.' And in the hadith of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, raising it: 'Allah reveals to the guardians: Do not write anything upon My servant at the time of his distress.'
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage explains the theological ruling on the recording of even involuntary sounds such as moans during illness. The author defines 'dhuhul' (forgetfulness) as oblivion and heedlessness. Then he states that the angels write even the moan (anīn) that emanates naturally from a person during sickness, as transmitted by the imams, especially Imam Malik, who is cited as one who held this view. The proof is the generality of the word 'qawl' (word) in the verse 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), since negation implies universality: every word is recorded, including moans. The author then gives the linguistic definition of 'anīn' as a sound made by groaning, with masculine 'ānn' and feminine 'annah'. He then reports that it is written. However, he adds a recommended interpretation: the phrase 'even the moan in sickness' should be understood as referring to the case where the sick person has good deeds and acts of obedience (that he performed before illness), based on the hadith of Anas that during illness, one is credited with the good deeds he used to do. He also cites the hadith of Ali that Allah commands the angels not to write anything upon the servant during his distress (dajr). This shows that the recorded moan is interpreted in light of prior good deeds, not as a mere involuntary utterance.

Key Terms
الذهول (forgetfulness)
الأنين (moan)
المرض (sickness)
العموم (generality)
قول (word)
الحفظة (guardians)
الضجر (distress)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All involuntary sounds are recorded unconditionally.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the hadith about not writing during distress limits this; the moan is recorded only in conjunction with prior good deeds.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof used for the recording of even the moan in sickness?
A) The consensus of the scholars
B) The generality of the word 'qawl' in the verse
C) The hadith of Anas
D) The definition of anin

Key Takeaway
The recording of moans is established by the generality of the verse, but the hadith conditions it to those with prior good deeds, showing Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever stop to think that your deepest, most hidden moments of agony—the moans no one else hears—are known to Allah and recorded by His angels? How does that reality change the way you view your private struggles? Will you now turn those groanings into a conversation with Him, knowing He hears even what you cannot put into words?
?
When you are in distress, do you remember that Allah commands the angels to withhold the pen? How does that mercy affect your attitude toward your trials? Can you trust that in your weakness, He is not tallying your faults but rather writing down the good deeds you used to do? Will you let that transform your distress into hope?
?
If your moans are only recorded as part of your prior righteousness, what does that reveal about the urgency of building a record of obedience before calamity strikes? Are you investing in deeds that will accompany you even when you are unable to speak or act? What will your moans say about you on the Day of Judgment?

The Recording Angels Write Every Word, Even a Groan
Explanation of the recording angels writing each word, including the groan in illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the recording angels write every word a person utters, including involuntary sounds like groans during illness, based on Quranic evidence and hadiths that also show divine mercy.

Core Idea
Every word you utter is recorded — even a groan.

This lesson examines the scope of the recording angels' writing. The commentator explains that based on the Quranic verse 'He does not utter a word except that there is with him an observer, ready' (Q. 50:18), scholars concluded that all speech, even involuntary groans, is recorded. However, there are exceptions of divine mercy. We will explore the evidence and the nuanced understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage without analysis, then the English translation to get the overall meaning.
2
Identify key terms
Locate the words ذهول and أنين and understand their definitions as given in the passage.
These are foundational for the lesson.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine how the verse 'مَا يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ' is used to prove generality.
Negative context implies all words.
4
Note the hadith exceptions
Understand the two hadiths: one about writing good deeds during illness, and one about not recording during distress.
Shows balance of justice and mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
والذهول عن الشيء: نسيانه والغفلة عنه.
يكتبون عليه (حَتَّى الأَنينَ) الصادر عن طبيعته (فِي المَرَض) هذا التّعميم في الكتابة (كَمَا نُقِلْ) أي: نقله أئمةُ الدِّين وعلماء المسلمين وقالوا به، ومن أعظمهم الإمام مالك الله ، ومثله لا يُقال بالرأي ، تمسكوا بقوله تعالى: مَا يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ ) [ق: ١٨]، إذ وقوع «قول» في سياق النَّفي يقتضي العُموم .
والأنين : مصدر أَنَّ الرَّجل ييْنُ [؟] بالكسر أنينا وأنانا – بالضم - صوَّتَ ؛ فالذَّكَرُ : آن، على فاعل، والأُنثى: أَنَّةٌ.
أَنَّه يُكتب
وينبغي حمل قوله: حتّى الأنين في المرض على معنى له في مرضه خيرات وطاعات؛ لما في حديث أنس ، قال: رسول الله : «إذا ابتلي الله العبد ببلاء في جَسدِه ؛ قال الله للملك : اكتب له صالح عمله الذي كان يعمله ؛ فإن شفاه .. غسله وطهره، وإن قبضه غفر له وفي حديث عليّ الله رفعه: (يُوحِي الله إلى الحَفَظَة: لا تكتبوا على عبدي عِندَ ضَجَرِه شيئًا ) .
Section of the Samʿiyyāt. Forgetfulness of a thing: its omission and heedlessness of it. They write upon him [even] the groan emanating from his nature during illness. This generalization in writing (as was transmitted) means: the imams of the religion and the Muslim scholars transmitted it and said it, and among the greatest of them is Imam Mālik (may Allah have mercy on him), and the like is not said by opinion. They adhered to His statement, the Exalted: 'He does not utter a word except that there is with him an observer, ready' [Q. 50:18], because the occurrence of 'word' in a negative context necessitates generality. And al-anīn is the verbal noun of anna al-rajul (to moan), with kasrah [pronounced] yainu, meaning to make a sound; the masculine is ānn, on the pattern of fāʿil, and the feminine is annah. That it is written. And it is necessary to interpret his saying: 'even the groan during illness' as meaning he has good deeds and acts of obedience during his illness, because of the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'When Allah tests a servant with a trial in his body, Allah says to the angel: Write for him the righteous deeds he used to do; then if He heals him, He washes and purifies him, and if He takes him, He forgives him.' And in the hadith of ʿAlī (may Allah be pleased with him) raised to the Prophet: 'Allah reveals to the guardians: Do not write upon My servant during his distress anything.'
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of the recording angels' writing, emphasizing that every utterance is recorded, even an involuntary groan during illness. The author begins by explaining the term 'al-dhuhūl' (forgetfulness) as omission and negligence. He then states that the angels write even the groan that naturally occurs in illness, citing that this was transmitted by the early imams, especially Imam Mālik, and is not based on mere opinion. They support this with the Qur'anic verse (50:18) which uses the general term 'word' in a negative context, implying all words are recorded. The author then discusses the word 'al-anīn' (groan), defining it as a sound from the throat. He then recommends interpreting the phrase 'even the groan during illness' as referring to a state where the person has good deeds during illness, citing a hadith from Anas that when a servant is afflicted, Allah commands the angel to write the good deeds he used to do, and either purifies him through recovery or forgives him upon death. A second hadith from ʿAlī states that Allah tells the guardian angels not to write anything when the servant is distressed, showing mercy. The passage thus clarifies the general rule of recording all words, with an exception for distress.

الرقيب العتيد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only deliberate or major speech is recorded by the angels.
Correction: The Quranic verse and teaching of the imams show that every word, even an involuntary groan, is recorded, except during distress.

D) The consensus of scholars that every sound is sinful.

Key Takeaway
The recording angels record every utterance, including involuntary sounds, based on the generality of Quran 50:18, but Allah's mercy exempts moments of distress.

?
You will be held accountable for every word. What would your angel's record look like for the last conversation you had? Are you prepared to meet that record?

Self-Accounting (Muḥāsabat al-Nafs)
Commentary on the command to take the soul to account.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose and benefit of holding oneself accountable in light of the recording angels.

Core Idea
Self-accounting eases the Hereafter reckoning.

The poem commands us to take our souls to account, especially knowing that angels record our deeds. This lesson explores the rationale and reward of self-accounting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on self-accounting
Read the Arabic passage from 'fidhā ʿalimta' to 'hāna ʿalayhi ḥisāb al-ākhira'. Let the call to accountability sink in.
Notice the two purposes mentioned.
2
Identify the two purposes
The passage gives two reasons for self-accounting: to give the angels rest and to ensure actions are done with knowledge of Allah's judgment.
3
Reflect on the benefit
The passage promises that whoever takes his soul to account in this world will find the reckoning of the Hereafter easy.
This connects self-accounting to eschatological reward.

في وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة
۸۷ - فَحَاسِبِ النَّفْسَ وقَلَّلْ الَامَلَا (۱) فرُبَّ مَنْ جَدَّ لِأَمْرِ وَصَلَا
وإذا علمتَ أنَّ عليك من يحفظ أعمالك ويكتبها (فَحَاسِبِ النَّفْسَ)(٢) ، أي : نفسكَ ؛ لتُرِيحَ الملائكة مِن التَّعب ، فتحاسبها على كل فعل قبل القدوم عليه، حتّى لا تتلبس به إلا بعد معرفة حكم الله فيه ؛ لأنَّ مَن حاسب نفسه الدُّنيا هان عليه حِساب الآخرة (وَقَلَّلْ)، أي: قَصِّر (الأَمَلَا) وهو: رجاءُ ما تُحبُّه النَّفس ، كطول عمر ، وزيادةِ غِنّى ، وهو مذموم إلا العلماء (۳) ، والأصل في هذا قوله : كُن في الدُّنيا كأنَّكَ غَرِيبٌ أو عَابِر سَبيل، وعدَّ مِن أهل القبور) (٤) ، فَرُبَّ مَنْ جَدَّ لِأمْرِ) أي : لأَنَّهُ رُبَّ مَنِ اجتهد بتوفيق الله تعالى لتحصيل أمرٍ من أمور الآخرة أو الدُّنيا (وَصَلَا) إليه، لتقدير نفسك من
On the obligation of belief in the guardians and recorders of deeds from among the angels. 87 - So take your soul to account and reduce hope, for perhaps one who strives for an matter attains it. And when you know that there is over you one who preserves your deeds and writes them, then take your soul to account, i.e., your own soul, to give the angels rest from fatigue. So bring it to account for every action before undertaking it, so that you do not engage in it except after knowing Allah's judgment concerning it; because whoever takes his soul to account in this world, the reckoning of the Hereafter will be light for him. And 'reduce', i.e., shorten, hope, which is the expectation of what the soul desires, such as long life and increase of wealth, and it is blameworthy except for scholars. The basis of this is his saying: 'Be in this world as if you were a stranger or a passerby, and count yourself among the people of the graves.' For perhaps one who strives for a matter, i.e., because perhaps one who strives with Allah's success for the attainment of some matter of the Hereafter or this world attains it. For your estimation of yourself from...
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on verse 87 of the poem, which calls for self-accounting and reducing hope. The author explains that since one knows the recording angels are watching, one should hold one's soul accountable before acting, to avoid burdening the angels with unnecessary work and to ensure actions align with Allah's rulings. This self-accounting in the world eases the reckoning in the Hereafter. The term 'qallil al-amala' (reduce hope) means to shorten one's expectation of worldly desires like long life and wealth, and such hope is blameworthy except for scholars, who may hope for long life to benefit others. The author cites the prophetic hadith advising to live as a stranger or passerby and to consider oneself among the dead. Finally, he explains the phrase 'rubbamā jadda li-amrin waṣalā' as encouraging striving—one who strives with divine success attains his goal, whether in worldly or religious matters. The passage ends mid-sentence, continuing onto the next page.

Reducing Hope and Striving
Commentary on reducing hope and striving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper approach to hope and the importance of striving.

Core Idea
Blameworthy hope is shortened except for scholars; strive with divine support.

The poem continues with the command to reduce hope and then emphasizes striving. This lesson unpacks the nature of hope, the exception for scholars, and the prophetic guidance to live as a stranger, along with the promise that striving leads to attainment.

The Obligation of Faith in Death
States the obligation to believe in death with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in death is obligatory, based on scriptural evidence and its classification as an intellectually possible matter conveyed by revelation.

Core Idea
Death must be believed in because revelation confirms what reason deems possible.

This lesson introduces the first part of the chapter on sam'iyyāt (matters known through revelation). The author asserts that faith in death is obligatory, grounding this obligation in both Quranic verses and the rational principle that whatever is intellectually possible and conveyed by revelation must be accepted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on obligation
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice how the author presents the obligation as a subject-predicate construction.
The phrase 'wājibu īmānunā' is emphasized.
2
Identify the evidence
Look at the Quranic verses cited and the mention of many hadiths. Understand that death is among 'mujawwazāt al-ʿuqūl'.
What makes belief obligatory is that the Law has informed us of these possibilities.
3
Reflect on the rational category
Death is not rationally necessary nor impossible; it is possible. The Law's confirmation makes it obligatory to believe.
This is a key principle in Ash'ari theology: revelation determines obligation in matters of the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
حقيقةُ الموتِ وقبضُ الأرواح
۸۸ - وَوَاجِبْ إيمانُنَا بالموتِ ويَقْبِضُ الرُّوحَ رَسُولُ الموتِ
(وَوَاجِبُ إِيمَانُنا) - مُبتدأ وخبر (۱) ـ ، أي : تصديقنا (بِالمَوْتِ) ونزوله بكل ذي روح واجبٌ ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيْتُونَ ﴾ [الزمر: ٣٠] ، وكُلُّ نَفْسٍ ذَائِقَةُ الْمَوْتِ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۱۸۵] ، والأحاديثُ فيه كثيرةٌ ، ولأنَّه مِن ١٨٥] مُجَوَّزَات (۲) العُقول التي وردَ الشَّرعُ بها ؛ فوجب اعتقادها .
ومذهب إمامنا الأشعري رحمه الله تعالى: أنَّ الموتَ كيفيَّةٌ وجودية (۳)
Section on Sam'iyyat: The reality of death and the taking of souls. 88 - And obligatory is our faith in death, and the messenger of death takes the soul. 'And obligatory is our faith' – subject and predicate – i.e., our affirmation of death and its descent upon every living soul is obligatory; because of His statement, the Most High: 'Indeed, you are to die, and indeed they are to die' [Az-Zumar: 30], and 'Every soul will taste death' [Aal-e-Imran: 185]; and the hadiths about it are many, and because it is among the intellectually possible [mujawwazāt] matters that the Law has conveyed; so it is obligatory to believe in them. And the school of our Imam al-Ashʿari, may God have mercy on him, is that death is a positive quality (kayfiyyah wujūdiyyah).
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on sam'iyyāt (matters known through revelation). It is a commentary on the verse: 'And obligatory is our faith in death, and the messenger of death takes the soul' (wa wājibu īmānunā bil-mawti wa yaqbiḍu ar-rūḥa rasūlu al-mawt). The commentator explains that the phrase 'obligatory is our faith' (wājibu īmānunā) is a subject and predicate construction meaning that our affirmation (taṣdīq) of death and its descent upon every living soul is obligatory. The proof is given from the Qur'an (Az-Zumar 30 and Aal-e-Imran 185) and many hadiths. The reason it is obligatory to believe is that death is among the intellectually possible (mujawwazāt al-ʿuqūl) matters that the Law (al-sharʿ) has conveyed; therefore, it is obligatory to believe in them. Then the commentator states the school of Imam al-Ashʿari: that death is a positive quality (kayfiyyah wujūdiyyah) – i.e., a real attribute that exists in the deceased, not merely the absence of life. This contrasts with the view that death is pure non-existence. The term 'positive' (wujūdiyyah) indicates that death can be perceived by sight, and the relationship between death and life is one of opposition (taḍādd).

تصديق

Key Takeaway
Belief in death is obligatory because revelation confirms what is rationally possible.

Death as a Positive Quality in Ash'ari Theology
States the Ash'ari doctrine that death is a positive quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that death is a positive quality (kayfiyyah wujūdiyyah), not mere annihilation.

Core Idea
In Ash'ari theology, death is a real created attribute, not the absence of life.

After establishing the obligation to believe in death, the author presents the specific Ash'ari doctrine: death is a 'positive quality' (kayfiyyah wujūdiyyah). This distinguishes the Ash'ari view from those who consider death as pure non-existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the line: 'ومذهب إمامنا الأشعري... أنَّ الموتَ كيفيَّةٌ وجودية'.
2
Understand 'kayfiyyah wujūdiyyah'
This term means death is a real attribute that exists in the deceased, not merely the absence of life. It can be perceived and has a positive existence.
Contrast with the view that death is pure non-existence.
3
Note the implications
If death is a positive quality, then it is a created entity that Allah brings about. This aligns with the Ash'ari emphasis on the reality of all attributes.
This also affects discussions on the intermediate state (barzakh).

The Obligation to Believe in Death
Al-Laqqani states the obligation to believe in death and provides evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in death is obligatory and how it is a contingent matter from the intellect that the Law has brought.

Core Idea
Belief in death is obligatory because it is rationally contingent and textually affirmed.

Al-Laqqani begins by establishing the necessity of believing in death. He grounds this in clear Quranic verses and the fact that death is among the contingent possibilities that reason acknowledges and revelation confirms. This lesson clarifies that obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Notice the structure: it begins with a section heading, then the statement of obligation.
The passage is part of the Sam'iyyat section, which deals with matters known through revelation.
2
Identify the proofs
Look for the evidence Al-Laqqani provides: Quranic verses and the rational category of contingent matters (mujawwazat).
The verses are 'Indeed, you are mortal...' and 'Every soul will taste death.'
3
Understand the concept of mujawwazat
Reflect on the idea that death is a rationally possible event that revelation confirms, making belief in it obligatory.
This distinguishes it from matters that are rationally necessary or impossible.

(۱) قوله: (مبتدأ وخبر) أي: على التقديم والتأخير . الشنواني. وقوله: (بالموت) يعني بعمومه، وفناء الكل كما نبه عليه الشارح ردا على الدهريَّة الذين قالوا: «أرحام تدفع وأرض تبلع». أو المُراد: الموتُ على الوجه المعهود شرعا من تقدير الآجال، لا كما قالت الحكماء: إنه بمجرد اختلال الطبيعة وتلاشي المزاج. وأما أصل وقوع الموت فمُشاهدٌ لا يشك فيه عاقل فلا حاجة للنص عليه ، وفي كلام الحسن: ما رأيت يقينا أشبه بالباطل من الموت». أراد: يتيقنه الإنسان ولا يتهيأ له ؛ فكأنه يكذبه. الأمير والشنواني.

Section on the Sam'iyyat. The reality of death and the seizing of souls. 88 - And our belief in death is obligatory, and the Angel of Death seizes the soul. (And our belief is obligatory) is a subject and predicate, i.e., our affirmation of death and its descent upon every possessor of a soul is obligatory; due to His statement: 'Indeed, you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' [az-Zumar:30], and 'Every soul will taste death' [Aal Imran:185], and the traditions on it are many, and because it is among contingent matters (mujawwazat) of the intellect that the Law has brought; so belief in it is obligatory. And the doctrine of our Imam al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) is that death is an existential quality (kayfiyya wujudiyya). (1) His saying: (subject and predicate) i.e., with تقديم وتأخير. Al-Shanwani. And his saying: (by death) means by its generality, and the annihilation of all, as the commentator pointed out in refutation of the materialists who said: 'Wombs expel and earth swallows.' Or the intended meaning is death in the legally familiar sense of decreed terms, not as the philosophers said: that it is merely the disruption of nature and the dissolution of temperament. As for the actual occurrence of death, it is witnessed, no rational person doubts it, so there is no need for textual evidence. And in the saying of al-Hasan: 'I have never seen a certainty more resembling falsehood than death.' He meant: a person is certain of it yet does not prepare for it, as if he denies it. Al-Amir and al-Shanwani. (2) His saying: (from مجوزات) with فتح of the waw, is a passive participle, and it is not correct in the form of an active participle; because the active participle is not added to its raised object, lest it entail adding a thing to itself, which is invalid, unlike the passive participle. Al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (existential quality) i.e., an attribute subsisting in the dead person, and his saying: (existential) i.e., it can be seen by the eye. In that case, the opposition between it and life is the opposition of contradiction. And evidence that it is existential is His statement: 'He who created death and life' [al-Mulk:2], and creating is bringing into existence and extracting from non-existence to existence, so death is existential. And the doctrine of al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari is that it is the absence of life from that which is capable of life, so it is the absence of a property of life; accordingly, the opposition between it and life is the opposition of absence and property. And some interpreted 'خَلَقَ' in the verse as meaning 'ordained', which is more general than bringing into existence, since non-existence can be ordained. And if it is conceded that it means bringing into existence, it is permissible that what is meant by 'creating death' is creating its causes, or that an implied addition is assumed. And that is not rare in speech. It was refuted that all of this is contrary to the apparent meaning, and there is no necessity calling for it, so it must be avoided. And al-Isfarayini interpreted death in the verse as the Hereafter, and life as this world, based on what was narrated from Ibn Abbas of that interpretation. All of that is contrary to the apparent meaning, and texts must be taken according to their apparent meanings unless there is evidence. And some scholars hesitated as to whether, on the view that it is existential, it is a substance or an accident. I say: The explicit statement of al-Ash'ari is that it is an accident. End. Al-Shanwani and al-Amir. In summary, death is an attribute of the dead person; so what is in the commentary of the author and others that death is a meaning in the hand of the Angel of Death, or its depiction as a ram, all is in consideration of causes and representation. And stopping and delegating in such matters is better. And I have indicated something of its essence in my book 'Ibtisam al-Azhar'.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. It begins by establishing the obligation to believe in death, citing Quranic verses and rational contingency. Then it presents the Ash'ari definition of death as an existential quality (kayfiyya wujudiyya), contrasting it with the view of some philosophers and the Mu'tazila that it is pure non-existence. The commentary explains that death is an attribute subsisting in the dead person, visible in principle, and opposite to life by contradiction. It provides evidence from the verse 'He who created death and life', interpreting 'creation' as bringing into existence, thus making death existential. It also discusses alternative interpretations and refutes them, insisting on the apparent meaning. The passage concludes by noting that death is an accident ('ard) according to al-Ash'ari, and that pictorial representations are merely metaphorical.

Key Terms
الموت
مجوزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That death is a purely physical event that needs no belief; some might think it is self-evident and not a matter of faith.
Correction: The passage shows that while death is witnessed, belief in it as part of divine decree and its universal application is an obligatory act of faith, supported by both reason and revelation.

The Ash'ari Definition of Death as an Existential Quality
Al-Laqqani states the Ash'ari definition of death as an existential quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Ash'ari doctrine death is an existential quality opposite to life, not mere non-existence.

Core Idea
Death is an existential attribute, not non-existence.

Al-Laqqani presents the Ash'ari position on the nature of death, defining it as an existential quality (kayfiyya wujudiyya) that subsists in the dead person. This lesson examines the evidence from the Quran and the implications for the relationship between death and life.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic statement: 'The doctrine of our Imam al-Ash'ari is that death is an existential quality.' Notice the key terms.
The term 'kayfiyya wujudiyya' means an attribute that exists in reality, not a mere absence.
2
Examine the evidence
The evidence is from Quran 67:2 'He who created death and life'. Understand how the word 'created' implies bringing into existence, making death something existent.
This is contrasted with the view that death is the absence of life.
3
Review alternative views
Note the alternative interpretations (e.g., 'created' means 'ordained', or death is absence) and why they are rejected as contrary to the apparent meaning.
The passage insists on the apparent meaning unless there is compelling evidence to deviate.

حقيقةُ الموتِ وقبضُ الأرواح
۸۸ - وَوَاجِبْ إيمانُنَا بالموتِ ويَقْبِضُ الرُّوحَ رَسُولُ الموتِ
(وَوَاجِبُ إِيمَانُنا) - مُبتدأ وخبر (۱) ـ ، أي : تصديقنا (بِالمَوْتِ) ونزوله بكل ذي روح واجبٌ ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيْتُونَ ﴾ [الزمر: ٣٠] ، وكُلُّ نَفْسٍ ذَائِقَةُ الْمَوْتِ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۱۸۵] ، والأحاديثُ فيه كثيرةٌ ، ولأنَّه مِن مُجَوَّزَات (۲) العُقول التي وردَ الشَّرعُ بها ؛ فوجب اعتقادها .
ومذهب إمامنا الأشعري رحمه الله تعالى: أنَّ الموتَ كيفيَّةٌ وجودية (۳)
(۱) قوله: (مبتدأ وخبر) أي: على التقديم والتأخير . الشنواني. وقوله: (بالموت) يعني بعمومه، وفناء الكل كما نبه عليه الشارح ردا على الدهريَّة الذين قالوا: «أرحام تدفع وأرض تبلع». أو المُراد: الموتُ على الوجه المعهود شرعا من تقدير الآجال، لا كما قالت الحكماء: إنه بمجرد اختلال الطبيعة وتلاشي المزاج. وأما أصل وقوع الموت فمُشاهدٌ لا يشك فيه عاقل فلا حاجة للنص عليه ، وفي كلام الحسن: ما رأيت يقينا أشبه بالباطل من الموت». أراد: يتيقنه الإنسان ولا يتهيأ له ؛ فكأنه يكذبه. الأمير والشنواني.
(۲) قوله: (من مجوزات) بفتح الواو ، اسم مفعول ، ولا يصح بلفظ اسم الفاعل ؛ لأن اسم الفاعل لا يضاف إلى مرفوعه ، لئلا يلزم إضافة الشيء لنفسه ، وهي لا تصح ، بخلاف اسم المفعول،
قال في الخلاصة:
وقد يضاف ذا إلى اسم مرتفع
الشنواني.
(۳) قوله: (كيفية وجودية) أي صفة قائمة بالميت، وقوله: (وجودية) أي: يمكن أن تُرى بالبصر، وحينئذ فالتقابل بينه وبين الحياة من تقابل التضاد، ويدل لكونه وجوديا قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِى خَلَقَ الْمَوْتَ وَالْحَيَوَةَ﴾ [الملك: ۲] وهو الإيجاد والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون الموت وجوديا، ومذهب الأستاذ الإسفراييني والزمخشري: أنه عدم الحياة عما الحياة ؛ فيكون عدم ملكة للحياة، وعليه فالتقابل بينه وبين الحياة من تقابل العدم والملكة
من
وأُول (خَلَقَ) في الآية بمعنى التقدير، وهو أعم من الإيجاد، إذ العدم يقدر ، ولو سُلَّمَ كونه بمعنى الإيجاد .. جازَ أن يُراد بخلق الموت إيجاد أسبابه ، أو يقدر المضاف ، وذلك غير عزيز في الكلام، وردَّ بأنَّ هذا كله خلاف الظاهر ، ولا ضرورة تدعو إليه؛ فيجب اجتنابه ، وأوَّلَ الأستاذ الموتَ فى الآية بالآخرة ، والحياة فيها بالدنيا ، مستندا لما روي عن ابن عباس من تفسيرها بذلك ، والكل خلاف الظاهر، والنصوص يجب أن تجري على ظواهرها إلا لقرينة ، وتوقف بعض العلماء على القول بأنه وجودي هل هو جوهر أو عرض ؟ قلت: صريح كلام الشيخ الأشعري على أنه عرض . اهـ . الشنواني الأمير وبالجملة الموتُ صفة للميت ، فما في شرح المصنف وغيره من أن الموت معنى في كف ملك الموت، أو تصويره بكبش ، كله باعتبار الأسباب والتمثيل، والوقفُ والتفويض في أمثال هذه المقامات

وقد أشرتُ إلى شيءٍ مِن لُبابه بكتابي : ابتسام الأزهار».
Section on the Sam'iyyat. The reality of death and the seizing of souls. 88 - And our belief in death is obligatory, and the Angel of Death seizes the soul. (And our belief is obligatory) is a subject and predicate, i.e., our affirmation of death and its descent upon every possessor of a soul is obligatory; due to His statement: 'Indeed, you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' [az-Zumar:30], and 'Every soul will taste death' [Aal Imran:185], and the traditions on it are many, and because it is among contingent matters (mujawwazat) of the intellect that the Law has brought; so belief in it is obligatory. And the doctrine of our Imam al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) is that death is an existential quality (kayfiyya wujudiyya). (1) His saying: (subject and predicate) i.e., with تقديم وتأخير. Al-Shanwani. And his saying: (by death) means by its generality, and the annihilation of all, as the commentator pointed out in refutation of the materialists who said: 'Wombs expel and earth swallows.' Or the intended meaning is death in the legally familiar sense of decreed terms, not as the philosophers said: that it is merely the disruption of nature and the dissolution of temperament. As for the actual occurrence of death, it is witnessed, no rational person doubts it, so there is no need for textual evidence. And in the saying of al-Hasan: 'I have never seen a certainty more resembling falsehood than death.' He meant: a person is certain of it yet does not prepare for it, as if he denies it. Al-Amir and al-Shanwani. (2) His saying: (from مجوزات) with فتح of the waw, is a passive participle, and it is not correct in the form of an active participle; because the active participle is not added to its raised object, lest it entail adding a thing to itself, which is invalid, unlike the passive participle. Al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (existential quality) i.e., an attribute subsisting in the dead person, and his saying: (existential) i.e., it can be seen by the eye. In that case, the opposition between it and life is the opposition of contradiction. And evidence that it is existential is His statement: 'He who created death and life' [al-Mulk:2], and creating is bringing into existence and extracting from non-existence to existence, so death is existential. And the doctrine of al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari is that it is the absence of life from that which is capable of life, so it is the absence of a property of life; accordingly, the opposition between it and life is the opposition of absence and property. And some interpreted 'خَلَقَ' in the verse as meaning 'ordained', which is more general than bringing into existence, since non-existence can be ordained. And if it is conceded that it means bringing into existence, it is permissible that what is meant by 'creating death' is creating its causes, or that an implied addition is assumed. And that is not rare in speech. It was refuted that all of this is contrary to the apparent meaning, and there is no necessity calling for it, so it must be avoided. And al-Isfarayini interpreted death in the verse as the Hereafter, and life as this world, based on what was narrated from Ibn Abbas of that interpretation. All of that is contrary to the apparent meaning, and texts must be taken according to their apparent meanings unless there is evidence. And some scholars hesitated as to whether, on the view that it is existential, it is a substance or an accident. I say: The explicit statement of al-Ash'ari is that it is an accident. End. Al-Shanwani and al-Amir. In summary, death is an attribute of the dead person; so what is in the commentary of the author and others that death is a meaning in the hand of the Angel of Death, or its depiction as a ram, all is in consideration of causes and representation. And stopping and delegating in such matters is better. And I have indicated something of its essence in my book 'Ibtisam al-Azhar'.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. It begins by establishing the obligation to believe in death, citing Quranic verses and rational contingency. Then it presents the Ash'ari definition of death as an existential quality (kayfiyya wujudiyya), contrasting it with the view of some philosophers and the Mu'tazila that it is pure non-existence. The commentary explains that death is an attribute subsisting in the dead person, visible in principle, and opposite to life by contradiction. It provides evidence from the verse 'He who created death and life', interpreting 'creation' as bringing into existence, thus making death existential. It also discusses alternative interpretations and refutes them, insisting on the apparent meaning. The passage concludes by noting that death is an accident ('ard) according to al-Ash'ari, and that pictorial representations are merely metaphorical.

تقابل التضاد
عدم الحياة

Correction: Death is an attribute that exists in the dead person, not nothingness.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah explicitly says He created death just as He created life. If death is a real created entity that you will encounter, how does this change the way you prepare for it daily? What specific action will you take today to acknowledge death's reality?
?
The Ash'aris argue that death is an existential quality, not merely the absence of life. If death has its own positive existence, then your life is not just a countdown to nothingness but a transition to another created state. Are you living as if death is an event you will experience, or as if it's an end? What worldly attachments do you need to sever right now?
?
If your very death is a creation of Allah, then every moment after death is also under His control. Does your faith in the afterlife reflect this certainty, or do you still harbor doubts about what comes next? Make a concrete intention today to study one verse about resurrection and act upon it.

The Seizing of Souls by the Angel of Death
Al-Laqqani explains the obligation to believe that the Angel of Death seizes souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe that the Angel of Death seizes all souls, including those of martyrs and all creatures, by God's permission.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death seizes every soul, from human to mosquito, by God's command.

This lesson covers a specific article of faith in the Samiyyat category: the belief in the Angel of Death and his role in taking souls. Al-Laqqani states it is obligatory to believe that he seizes the soul from its abode, and the commentary expands this to include all living beings. Let's examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of the matn and the detailed explanation in the commentary.
The matn is the first part before the comma; the rest is the sharh.
2
Identify the key elements
Who seizes the soul? From where? By whose permission? Which souls are included? Locate these in the text.
The text mentions 'from its abode or from the hands of his assistants'.
3
Reflect on the universal scope
The passage explicitly lists categories: humans, jinn, angels, beasts, birds, and even a mosquito. Consider why such detail is given.
This emphasizes God's absolute sovereignty over life and death.

Source Text

(و) واجبٌ إيمَانُنا أيضًا بأنَّهُ: يَقْبِضُ الرُّوحَ ) ، أي : يُخرِجُها ويأخُذها بإذن ربه مِن مَقرّها أو من يد أعوَانِه ، ولو أرواح الشهداء ، برا وبحرا ، والمراد: جميعُ أرواحِ التَّقلينِ والمَلائكة والبهائم والطير وغيرهم ولو بعوضة.
(And) our belief is also obligatory that he (the Angel of Death) seizes the soul, i.e., he extracts it and takes it by the permission of his Lord from its abode or from the hands of his assistants, even the souls of martyrs, on land and sea, and the intent is all souls of the two weighty ones (humans and jinn) and angels and beasts and birds and others, even a mosquito.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage defines the belief in the Angel of Death seizing souls. It begins with the matn line stating that it is obligatory to believe that the Angel of Death seizes the soul. The commentary then explains the process: he extracts the soul from its abode or from the hands of his assistants, by God's permission. This includes all souls, even those of martyrs, and extends to all created beings: humans, jinn, angels, animals, birds, and even a mosquito. This universal scope emphasizes the power of God and the comprehensiveness of death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Angel of Death seizes every soul, including yours, at a moment you cannot predict. Are you living today as if that moment is imminent? What would you change if you knew your soul would be seized tonight?
?
Even the soul of a mosquito is taken with precise divine permission. If Allah does not overlook even a mosquito, what makes you think He will overlook your deliberate sins? Which sin are you currently excusing that demands immediate repentance?
?
The passage includes martyrs in the grasp of death. You may hope for honor in the afterlife, but are you prepared for the moment of death right now, in your current state of faith? What is the one action you can take today to ensure you meet Allah with sincerity?

The Reality of Death and Its Universal Scope
Defines death and its universal scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of death as a transition and the obligation to believe that God takes all souls.

Core Idea
Death is not annihilation but a transfer, and all souls return to God.

This lesson begins by establishing the true nature of death in Islamic theology. Death is often misunderstood as pure non-existence, but the author clarifies that it is the cessation of the soul's attachment to the body and a transition to the next life. The passage also emphasises that God is the one who takes every soul, from humans to animals, highlighting the universal sovereignty of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of death
Read carefully the first sentences describing death as opposite to life and not pure non-existence. Notice the key phrases: 'انقطاع تعلق الروح بالبدن' and 'تبدل حال وانتقال من دار إلى دار'.
The hadith of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz reinforces the idea of transfer.
2
Understand the universal scope of death
Read the part about God taking all souls, including angels, jinn, animals, etc. Reflect on the comprehensiveness.
This includes even the smallest creatures like mosquitoes.
3
Reflect on the purpose of this lesson
Consider why this definition matters for theology: it establishes that death is a created reality, not a mere absence.
This prepares for the next lesson on the existential dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حقيقة الموتِ وقبضُ الأرواح تُضادُّ الحياةَ ، فلا يعرى الجسم الحيواني عنهما، ولا يجتمعان فيه، وليس بعدم محض ولا فناء صرف ، وإِنَّما هو انقطاع تعلقِ الرُّوحِ بالبدنِ ، ومفارقة وحيلولةٌ بينهما، وتبدل حال ،بحال وانتقال مِن دارٍ إلى دار ، وفي حديث عمر بن عبد العزيز: «إنَّما خُلِقتم للأبد، ولكنكم تنتقلون من دارٍ إلى دار» وقد أشرتُ إلى شيءٍ مِن لُبابه بكتابي : ابتسام الأزهار. وواجبٌ إيمَانُنا أيضًا بأنَّهُ: يَقْبِضُ الرُّوحَ ، أي : يُخرِجُها ويأخُذها بإذن ربه مِن مَقرّها أو من يد أعوَانِه ، ولو أرواح الشهداء ، برا وبحرا ، والمراد: جميعُ أرواحِ التَّقلينِ والمَلائكة والبهائم والطير وغيرهم ولو بعوضة. شأنه الَّذِى خَلَقَ الْمَوْتَ وَالْحَيَوَةَ﴾ [الملك: ۲] وهو الإيجاد والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون الموت وجوديا، ومذهب الأستاذ الإسفراييني والزمخشري: أنه عدم الحياة عما الحياة ؛ فيكون عدم ملكة للحياة، وعليه فالتقابل بينه وبين الحياة من تقابل العدم والملكة. وأُول (خَلَقَ) في الآية بمعنى التقدير، وهو أعم من الإيجاد، إذ العدم يقدر ، ولو سُلَّمَ كونه بمعنى الإيجاد .. جازَ أن يُراد بخلق الموت إيجاد أسبابه ، أو يقدر المضاف ، وذلك غير عزيز في الكلام، وردَّ بأنَّ هذا كله خلاف الظاهر ، ولا ضرورة تدعو إليه؛ فيجب اجتنابه ، وأوَّلَ الأستاذ الموتَ فى الآية بالآخرة ، والحياة فيها بالدنيا ، مستندا لما روي عن ابن عباس من تفسيرها بذلك ، والكل خلاف الظاهر، والنصوص يجب أن تجري على ظواهرها إلا لقرينة ، وتوقف بعض العلماء على القول بأنه وجودي هل هو جوهر أو عرض ؟ قلت: صريح كلام الشيخ الأشعري على أنه عرض . وبالجملة الموتُ صفة للميت ، فما في شرح المصنف وغيره من أن الموت معنى في كف ملك الموت، أو تصويره بكبش ، كله باعتبار الأسباب والتمثيل، والوقفُ والتفويض في أمثال هذه المقامات أولى.
The reality of death and the taking of souls: it is opposite to life; the animal body is not free from the two, nor do they coexist in it. It is not pure non-existence nor absolute annihilation, but rather it is the cessation of the soul's attachment to the body, separation and partition between them, a change of state from one state to another, and a transfer from one abode to another. In the hadith of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'You were created for eternity, but you are transferred from one abode to another.' And I have indicated something of its core in my book 'Ibtisam al-Azhar'. And it is obligatory for our faith also that He takes the soul, i.e., He extracts it and takes it by the permission of his Lord from its place or from the hand of His assistants, even the souls of martyrs, on land and sea, and the intent is all souls of the two heavy ones (humans and jinn), angels, animals, birds, and others, even a mosquito. His affair: He who created death and life [Quran 67:2] and it is bringing into existence and extraction from non-existence to existence, so death is existential. The school of al-Ustadh al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari: it is the absence of life from that which is capable of life; so it is the absence of the faculty of life, and accordingly the opposition between it and life is the opposition of absence and faculty. And they interpreted 'created' in the verse as meaning 'decreed', which is more general than bringing into existence, since non-existence is decreed. And if it is conceded that it is in the sense of bringing into existence, then it is possible that by 'creation of death' is meant the bringing into existence of its causes, or the implied object is understood, and that is not uncommon in speech. But it was replied that all of this is contrary to the apparent meaning, and there is no necessity requiring it; so it must be avoided. And al-Ustadh interpreted death in the verse as the Hereafter, and life therein as this world, based on what was narrated from Ibn Abbas as its interpretation. But all is contrary to the apparent meaning, and texts must be taken according to their apparent meanings unless there is an indication. And some scholars hesitated about the statement that it is existential: is it a substance or an accident? I said: the explicit statement of Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that it is an accident. And in summary, death is an attribute of the dead. So what is in the explanation of the author and others that death is a meaning in the hand of the Angel of Death, or its depiction as a ram, all is on the basis of causes and representation, and stopping and delegating in such matters is better.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of death and addresses a theological dispute about its nature. It begins by stating that death is the opposite of life and explains that it is not mere non-existence but rather the cessation of the soul's attachment to the body. The author then quotes a hadith from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz to emphasize that death is a transition. Next, he affirms that faith requires believing that God takes all souls, including those of angels, humans, jinn, and even animals. The central theological issue is whether death is existential (a created attribute) or non-existential (absence of life). The author presents the view of al-Ash'ari that death is a created accident (ʿarad), and he critiques the interpretations of al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari who consider death as the absence of life. He argues that the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse supports the existential view, and that other interpretations are forced. He concludes that death is an attribute of the dead and that figurative interpretations should be avoided; instead, one should stop and delegate knowledge to God.

Key Takeaway
Death is not the end but a transition commissioned by God, affecting all living beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The hadith says you were created for eternity. Does your daily routine reflect that eternal perspective, or are you trapped in the illusion that this world is permanent? What one change will you make today to realign with the truth?
?
God takes every soul, even a mosquito's. Does this universal scope humble you? As you consider the countless creatures who die each moment, do you recognize your own insignificance and yet your unique accountability before the One who takes all souls?

The Existential Nature of Death: A Theological Dispute
Argues for death as existential and critiques non-existential views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate on whether death is existential (a created attribute) or non-existential (absence of life), and the Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
Death is a created accident, not a mere absence of life.

Building on the definition of death as a transition, this lesson delves into a key theological dispute: Is death itself an existential reality created by God, or is it merely the absence of life? The author presents the Ash'ari view, supported by the Quranic verse 'He who created death and life', and critiques alternative interpretations. This discussion highlights the principle of taking texts according to their apparent meaning unless there is a clear indication otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument for existential death
Read the verse and the author's interpretation: 'He who created death and life' implies death is something created, thus existential.
The author equates 'creation' with bringing into existence.
2
Examine the opposing view
Read the opinion of al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari, who consider death as the absence of life, i.e., the absence of a faculty.
This view interprets 'created' as 'decreed' or refers to creation of causes.
3
Understand the rejoinder
The author rejects these alternative interpretations as contrary to the apparent meaning and lacking necessity.
The principle: texts must be taken at face value unless there is a clear indicator.
4
Learn the Ash'ari conclusion
The author states that Shaykh al-Ash'ari explicitly said death is an accident (ʿarad), and that it is an attribute of the dead.
Figurative interpretations about the Angel of Death holding death as a ram are dismissed as metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حقيقة الموتِ وقبضُ الأرواح تُضادُّ الحياةَ ، فلا يعرى الجسم الحيواني عنهما، ولا يجتمعان فيه، وليس بعدم محض ولا فناء صرف ، وإِنَّما هو انقطاع تعلقِ الرُّوحِ بالبدنِ ، ومفارقة وحيلولةٌ بينهما، وتبدل حال ،بحال وانتقال مِن دارٍ إلى دار ، وفي حديث عمر بن عبد العزيز: «إنَّما خُلِقتم للأبد، ولكنكم تنتقلون من دارٍ إلى دار» وقد أشرتُ إلى شيءٍ مِن لُبابه بكتابي : ابتسام الأزهار. وواجبٌ إيمَانُنا أيضًا بأنَّهُ: يَقْبِضُ الرُّوحَ ، أي : يُخرِجُها ويأخُذها بإذن ربه مِن مَقرّها أو من يد أعوَانِه ، ولو أرواح الشهداء ، برا وبحرا ، والمراد: جميعُ أرواحِ التَّقلينِ والمَلائكة والبهائم والطير وغيرهم ولو بعوضة. شأنه الَّذِى خَلَقَ الْمَوْتَ وَالْحَيَوَةَ﴾ [الملك: ۲] وهو الإيجاد والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون الموت وجوديا، ومذهب الأستاذ الإسفراييني والزمخشري: أنه عدم الحياة عما الحياة ؛ فيكون عدم ملكة للحياة، وعليه فالتقابل بينه وبين الحياة من تقابل العدم والملكة. وأُول (خَلَقَ) في الآية بمعنى التقدير، وهو أعم من الإيجاد، إذ العدم يقدر ، ولو سُلَّمَ كونه بمعنى الإيجاد .. جازَ أن يُراد بخلق الموت إيجاد أسبابه ، أو يقدر المضاف ، وذلك غير عزيز في الكلام، وردَّ بأنَّ هذا كله خلاف الظاهر ، ولا ضرورة تدعو إليه؛ فيجب اجتنابه ، وأوَّلَ الأستاذ الموتَ فى الآية بالآخرة ، والحياة فيها بالدنيا ، مستندا لما روي عن ابن عباس من تفسيرها بذلك ، والكل خلاف الظاهر، والنصوص يجب أن تجري على ظواهرها إلا لقرينة ، وتوقف بعض العلماء على القول بأنه وجودي هل هو جوهر أو عرض ؟ قلت: صريح كلام الشيخ الأشعري على أنه عرض . وبالجملة الموتُ صفة للميت ، فما في شرح المصنف وغيره من أن الموت معنى في كف ملك الموت، أو تصويره بكبش ، كله باعتبار الأسباب والتمثيل، والوقفُ والتفويض في أمثال هذه المقامات أولى.
The reality of death and the taking of souls: it is opposite to life; the animal body is not free from the two, nor do they coexist in it. It is not pure non-existence nor absolute annihilation, but rather it is the cessation of the soul's attachment to the body, separation and partition between them, a change of state from one state to another, and a transfer from one abode to another. In the hadith of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'You were created for eternity, but you are transferred from one abode to another.' And I have indicated something of its core in my book 'Ibtisam al-Azhar'. And it is obligatory for our faith also that He takes the soul, i.e., He extracts it and takes it by the permission of his Lord from its place or from the hand of His assistants, even the souls of martyrs, on land and sea, and the intent is all souls of the two heavy ones (humans and jinn), angels, animals, birds, and others, even a mosquito. His affair: He who created death and life [Quran 67:2] and it is bringing into existence and extraction from non-existence to existence, so death is existential. The school of al-Ustadh al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari: it is the absence of life from that which is capable of life; so it is the absence of the faculty of life, and accordingly the opposition between it and life is the opposition of absence and faculty. And they interpreted 'created' in the verse as meaning 'decreed', which is more general than bringing into existence, since non-existence is decreed. And if it is conceded that it is in the sense of bringing into existence, then it is possible that by 'creation of death' is meant the bringing into existence of its causes, or the implied object is understood, and that is not uncommon in speech. But it was replied that all of this is contrary to the apparent meaning, and there is no necessity requiring it; so it must be avoided. And al-Ustadh interpreted death in the verse as the Hereafter, and life therein as this world, based on what was narrated from Ibn Abbas as its interpretation. But all is contrary to the apparent meaning, and texts must be taken according to their apparent meanings unless there is an indication. And some scholars hesitated about the statement that it is existential: is it a substance or an accident? I said: the explicit statement of Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that it is an accident. And in summary, death is an attribute of the dead. So what is in the explanation of the author and others that death is a meaning in the hand of the Angel of Death, or its depiction as a ram, all is on the basis of causes and representation, and stopping and delegating in such matters is better.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of death and addresses a theological dispute about its nature. It begins by stating that death is the opposite of life and explains that it is not mere non-existence but rather the cessation of the soul's attachment to the body. The author then quotes a hadith from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz to emphasize that death is a transition. Next, he affirms that faith requires believing that God takes all souls, including those of angels, humans, jinn, and even animals. The central theological issue is whether death is existential (a created attribute) or non-existential (absence of life). The author presents the view of al-Ash'ari that death is a created accident (ʿarad), and he critiques the interpretations of al-Isfarayini and al-Zamakhshari who consider death as the absence of life. He argues that the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse supports the existential view, and that other interpretations are forced. He concludes that death is an attribute of the dead and that figurative interpretations should be avoided; instead, one should stop and delegate knowledge to God.

العدمي

التقابل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That death is merely the absence of life, not something created.
Correction: The Ash'ari view, based on the Quran, is that death is a created accident.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct interpretation of 'He created death'?
A) He decreed death.
B) He brought death into existence from non-existence.
C) He created the causes of death.
D) He designated death as the Hereafter.

Key Takeaway
Death is a created accident, not a mere absence; textual interpretation should adhere to the apparent meaning unless necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that death is a created reality, not just an absence. If death is something Allah deliberately creates, how does that change the way you view your own mortality? Will you begin today to live with the awareness that death is a real appointment set by your Creator, not a mere end?
?
The scholars debated whether death is a substance or an accident. Do you treat death as an abstract idea that happens to others, or as a concrete event that will happen to you? What specific action can you take this week to make the reality of your own death more present in your daily choices?
?
The passage warns against interpreting the Quran away from its apparent meaning without necessity. Are there verses about death or the afterlife that you have explained away to avoid discomfort? Will you commit to accepting Allah's words as they are, even when they confront you with difficult truths?

The Name and Reality of the Angel of Death
Identifies the Angel of Death and refutes opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the name of the Angel of Death, its meaning, and the correct belief about the scope of his mission according to Sunni scholars.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death is Azrael, meaning 'servant of the Mighty', and he takes all souls.

This lesson introduces the Angel of Death, known as Azrael, and clarifies the Sunni position on his role. It also refutes the views of the Mu'tazila and innovators who restrict the souls he takes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation to understand the basic claims about the Angel of Death.
2
Identify the name and meaning
The passage states the Angel is called Azrael, meaning 'servant of the Mighty'. This is the view of Ahl al-Haqq.
3
Understand the refuted views
Note the Mu'tazila say he only takes souls of humans and jinn; the innovators say he does not take animal souls. The author refutes both using the definite article 'al' for generality.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does it matter that the Angel takes all souls? It emphasizes his vast role and that no soul escapes death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات رَسُولُ المَوْتِ عزرائيل ، ومعناه عبد الجبار ، كما ذهب إليه أهل الحقِّ ، خلافًا للمعتزلة ، حيث ذهبوا إلى أنَّه لا يقبضُ أرواحَ غيرِ الثَّقلين ، وللمبتدعة الذاهبين إلى أنَّه لا يقبض أرواح البهائم ، بل أعوانه، وأَشار إلى الرَّد على الجميع بـ«أل» الدَّالَّة على العموم وهُو مَلَكٌ عَظِيمٌ هائلُ المَنْظَرِ مُفزع جدًّا، رأسه في السَّماء العليا، ورجلاه في تخوم الأرض السفلى ، ووجهه مقابل اللوح المحفوظ ، والخَلْقُ بين عينيه ، وله أعوان بعدد من يموتُ ، يترفّق بالمؤمن ويأتيه في صورة حسنة ، دون غيره، ومجيء الموتِ والعبد على عمل صالح يُسهل الموتَ ، وكذا السواك فيما ذكره جماعة، واستدلوا بحديث عائشةَ في الصحيح في قِصَّة سواكه عند موته . وأمَّا إِسنادُ التّوفّي إليه تعالى في قوله: ﴿اللَّهُ يَتَوَفَّى الْأَنفُسَ حِينَ موتها﴾ الآية.
The section on transmitted matters. The messenger of death is Azrael, and its meaning is 'servant of the Mighty', as the people of truth hold, contrary to the Mu'tazila, who hold that he does not take the souls of other than the two heavy ones (humans and jinn), and contrary to the innovators who hold that he does not take the souls of animals, but rather his assistants. And he indicated the refutation of all by the 'al' which indicates generality. And he is a great angel, terrifying in appearance, extremely frightening. His head is in the highest heaven, and his feet in the depths of the lowest earth. His face is opposite the Preserved Tablet, and all creation is between his eyes. He has assistants equal to the number of those who die. He is gentle with the believer and comes to him in a beautiful form, unlike others. The coming of death while the servant is engaged in a righteous deed eases death, and likewise the siwak, as a group mentioned. They adduced the hadith of Aisha in the Sahih concerning the story of his siwak at the time of his death. As for attributing the taking of souls to Him, the Exalted, in His saying: 'Allah takes the souls at the time of their death' [Quran 39:42] etc.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a description of the angel of death and a refutation of opposing views. It begins by stating that the angel of death is named Azrael, meaning 'servant of the Mighty', and this is the position of the Ahl al-Haqq (Sunni scholars). It then contrasts this with the Mu'tazila, who believed that the angel only takes the souls of humans and jinn (the thaqalayn), and the innovators (mubtadi'a) who believed he does not take the souls of animals—rather, that his assistants do. The author points out that the use of the definite article 'al' in 'al-arwah' (the souls) indicates generality, refuting these restrictive views. The passage then describes the angel's enormous size: his head in the highest heaven, his feet in the lowest earth, his face facing the Preserved Tablet, and all creation between his eyes. He has a vast number of assistants. The angel is gentle with believers, coming to them in a beautiful form. The passage also notes that death is eased when one is engaged in a righteous deed, and mentions the siwak (tooth-stick) as a means of easing death, citing the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's siwak at death. Finally, it references the Quranic verse 'Allah takes the souls' to show that ultimately God is the one who causes death.

Key Terms
رَسُولُ المَوْتِ
عزرائيل
المعتزلة
المبتدعة
أل الدالة على العموم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Angel of Death only takes human souls.
Correction: He takes all souls, including animals, as indicated by the generalized 'al'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who holds that the Angel of Death does not take the souls of animals?
A) The Mu'tazila.
B) The innovators (mubtadi'a).
C) The people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq).
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The Angel of Death, Azrael, takes all souls, refuting those who limit his role.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul, every moment, is in the hands of the Angel of Death. Do you live today as if you will be held accountable for every breath? What is one thing you will change today to prepare for that meeting?
?
The Mu'tazila and innovators both limit the Angel of Death's role—do you ever unconsciously limit Allah's sovereignty over your life, thinking certain areas are outside His direct control? How will you surrender those areas today?
?
If you truly believed that Azrael himself takes every soul—even the smallest insect—would you treat every living thing with more reverence? What creature will you show extra mercy to today as a sign of that belief?

The Grandeur and Gentleness of the Angel of Death
Describes the Angel of Death's attributes, his treatment of believers, and the ease of death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the immense size and attributes of the Angel of Death, and understand how he treats believers with gentleness and how death is eased by good deeds.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death is a colossal being who acts with mercy toward believers and eases death for the righteous.

This lesson describes the physical majesty of the Angel of Death—his vast size, his face opposite the Preserved Tablet, and his countless assistants. It also details his compassion toward believers, the ease of death for those engaged in good works, and the practice of siwak at death, as exemplified by the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of his size
Read how the Angel's head is in the highest heaven, feet in the lowest earth, and his face opposite the Preserved Tablet.
This shows his enormity and closeness to Allah's decree.

He has assistants equal to the number of those who die. This highlights the scale of his task.
3
Understand his mercy to believers
He is gentle with the believer and comes in a beautiful form, unlike for others.
4
Learn the ease of death
Death is eased by righteous deeds and by using siwak. The hadith of Aisha is cited.
5
Contemplate the Quranic verse
The verse 'Allah takes the souls' shows that ultimately death is from Allah, while the Angel is the agent.
