The Sunni Doctrine of the Single Fixed Term (Ajal)
Doctrinal definition with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that every soul has a single, predetermined term (ajal) and that the killer has no causative role in the death of the slain.

Core Idea
The ajal is one and invariable; no killer can shorten it.

This lesson clarifies a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding life and death. The passage explains that every person, including those slain, dies exactly at their appointed time, known only to Allah. It addresses the misconception that a killer changes the victim's term, affirming that Allah's decree is fixed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Let the author's phrasing settle before analyzing.
Note the dense theological language; don't worry if it feels heavy at first.
2
Identify the core claims
Find the statements that: (1) the ajal is one without multiplicity, (2) every slain person dies at his term, (3) the killer has no involvement, (4) if not killed, the person could die at that time or not.
These are the pillars of the Sunni position.
3
Understand the evidence
Look at the Quranic verse cited (Yunus 49). Notice how it supports the idea that the term cannot be advanced or delayed.
The verse is the primary proof; other verses and hadith are alluded to.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this doctrine matters: it upholds divine predestination (qadar) and absolves the killer of causing the death in a ultimate sense.
This connects to deeper theological debates about free will and fate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات خبر قوله : (مَنْ يُقْتَلُ): المبتدأ ، أي : كلّ ذي روح يُفعل به ما يُزهق روحه ، يعني أنَّ مُختار أهل السُّنَّة: وجوب اعتقادِ أَنَّ الأَجلَ بحَسَب عِلْمِ اللهِ تَعالى واحدٌ لا تَعدُّدَ فيه، وأنَّ كُلَّ مَقْتُولٍ مَيِّتُ بسبب انقضاء عمره وعند حضور أجله، في الوقت الذي علم الله في الأزل حصول موته فيه بإيجاده تعالى وخلقه، من غير مدخليّة للقاتل فيه ، لا مباشرة ولا تولد ، وأنَّه لو لم يُقتل لجازَ أنْ يموتَ في ذلك الوقت وأن لا يموت ، من غير قطع بامتدادِ العمر ولا بالموت بدل القتل ، بدليل أنَّ الله تعالى قد حكم بآجال العباد على ما عَلم مِن غير تَردُّدٍ ، وأَنَّهُ إِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ فَلَا يَسْتَخِرُونَ سَاعَةً وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ) [يونس: ٤٩] ، في آياتٍ وأحاديثَ دالة على أنَّ كُلَّ هالك يَستَوفي أجلَهُ مِن غير تَقَدُّم عليه ولا تَأَخُرٍ عنه
بيان أن الأجل واحد والمقتول ميت بأجله
The section of sam'iyyat (audible matters). The report of His saying: 'Who is killed' is the subject. Meaning: every soul to whom something is done that causes his spirit to leave. That is, the chosen doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah is the obligation of believing that the term (ajal) according to the knowledge of God the Exalted is one without multiplicity therein, and that every slain person dies due to the expiration of his lifespan and at the presence of his term, at the time that God knew in pre-eternity the occurrence of his death therein by His bringing into existence and creation, without any involvement of the killer therein, neither directly nor by generation (tawallud), and that if he were not slain, it is possible that he would die at that time and that he would not die, without definite assertion of extension of life nor of death instead of killing, as evidence that God the Exalted has decreed the terms of the servants according to what He knew without hesitation, and that 'when their term comes, they cannot delay it an hour nor advance it' [Yunus:49], among verses and hadiths indicating that every perishing person completes his term without being ahead of it or behind it.
Statement that the term is one and the slain dies by his term.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement of the Sunni position on the single fixed term (ajal) for every soul. It begins by explaining a Quranic phrase ('man yugtal' – who is killed) to establish the subject: every soul that dies. Then it states the core belief: the ajal is one according to God's knowledge, with no multiplicity. Every slain person dies exactly at his appointed time, which God knew in pre-eternity, and the killer has no involvement, neither directly nor through generated causation (tawallud). Moreover, if he were not killed, it is possible he would die at that same time or not—meaning we cannot be certain that he would have lived longer. The evidence is from the Quran (Yunus 49) and other texts showing that death cannot be advanced or delayed. The passage concludes with a heading summarizing this doctrine.

Key Terms
السمعيات

المقتول
التولد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The killer cuts short the victim's life, altering the predestined term.
Correction: The Sunni view holds that the ajal is one and invariable; the killer does not cause death in an ultimate sense—Allah's decree is fixed.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni doctrine stated in this passage, what is the role of the killer in the death of the slain?
A) The killer directly causes death.
B) The killer generates death through his act.
C) The killer has no involvement in the death.
D) The killer determines the exact time of death.

Key Takeaway
Every soul dies at its fixed term; no external action can alter Allah's decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a murder or an accident, does your heart truly accept that the victim's term had come, no matter what the apparent cause? If not, what does that reveal about your trust in Allah's decree?
?
If you believe your death is fixed and unchangeable, what changes in the way you live your daily life? Are you living with the urgency of that fixed hour, or do you act as if you control your tomorrow?
?
The killer has no involvement in the victim's death. Do you hold any grudges against people who have wronged you, knowing that their actions could not have altered what Allah had written for you? Can you release that grudge now?

Unseen Matters
intermediate
6 min
Three Responses to the Hadith on Lifespan Increase
The author responds to the hadith about acts increasing lifespan with three explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about acts increasing lifespan is reconciled with the doctrine of a single fixed ajal through three distinct explanations.

Core Idea
The hadith on lifespan increase is reconciled without contradicting definitive proofs.

This passage deals with an apparent conflict between a hadith that says certain acts increase lifespan and the Quranic doctrine of a fixed, unchangeable ajal. The author, a Sunni theologian, offers three reconciliations that preserve the integrity of revealed truths. As you read, notice how each explanation addresses a different aspect of the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the challenge
The hadith about acts increasing lifespan appears to contradict the definitive proofs that ajal is fixed. Understand why this is a problem.
2
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the three explanations.
3
Distinguish the three explanations
The author gives three distinct responses. Notice the logical progression: epistemic (solitary hadith), interpretive (blessing), and theological (angels' record vs. God's knowledge).
4
Connect to Quran 13:39
The third explanation relies on the verse about erasing and confirming. See how this supports the reconciliation.
5
Reflect on the Sunni stance
Conclude that the people of truth uphold that only what God's eternal knowledge attaches to is what actually occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحديث : أنَّ بعض الطاعات يزيدُ في العمر .. لا يُعارِضُ القواطع ؛ لأنَّه خبر واحدٍ ، أو أنّ الزّيادة فيه بحسَب الخير والبركة ، أو بالنسبة إلى ما أثبتته الملائكة في صحفها ، فقد يُثبتُ فيها الشَّيء مُطلقا، وهو في علم الله تعالى مُقيَّدٌ ، ثم يؤول إلى موجب علمه سبحانه على ما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: يَمْحُوا اللَّهُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيُثْبِتُ وَعِندَهُ أُمُّ الْكِتَبِ ) [الرعد: ٣٩]، فالمعتبر إنما هو ما تعلَّق العلمُ الأزليُّ ببلوغه، هذا ما عليه أهل الحقِّ.
And the hadith that some acts of obedience increase in lifespan does not contradict the definitive proofs, because it is a solitary hadith (khabar wahid), or that the increase therein is in terms of good and blessing, or in relation to what the angels have recorded in their scrolls, for they may record something absolutely, while it is in the knowledge of God the Exalted as qualified, then it leads to what His knowledge necessitates, as indicated by His saying: 'Allah erases what He wills and confirms, and with Him is the Mother of the Book' [ar-Ra'd:39]. So what is considered is only what the eternal knowledge has attached to its attainment. This is what the people of truth hold.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage addresses an apparent objection to the doctrine of a fixed single ajal: a hadith states that some acts of obedience increase lifespan. The author gives three reconciliations. First, the hadith is solitary (khabar wahid), so it cannot override the definitive proofs (qawaati') from the Quran. Second, the 'increase' may refer to blessing and goodness in life, not length. Third, the angels record things absolutely in their scrolls (e.g., 'so-and-so will live fifty years'), but in God's knowledge it is conditional (e.g., 'if he performs a certain act, he will live sixty'). God's eternal knowledge ultimately determines what actually occurs, as per Quran 13:39. Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved, and the Sunni doctrine remains intact.

Key Terms
خبر واحد
الزيادة في العمر
أم الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Misunderstanding the hadith as proving that ajal is not fixed.
Correction: The hadith does not contradict the fixed ajal doctrine because it is solitary, interpreted as blessing, or understood in light of God's eternal knowledge.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the explanations given in this passage for the hadith on increase in lifespan?
A) The hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid).
B) The increase refers to good and blessing.
C) The increase refers to the number of children.
D) The increase is relative to what angels record.

Key Takeaway
The hadith on lifespan increase is reconciled with the fixed ajal through three explanations: epistemic, interpretive, and theological.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of worship, do you ever find yourself expecting a tangible reward like a longer life? How does the lesson's explanation of 'increase in lifespan' as blessing challenge your motivation to worship purely for Allah's sake?
?
How often do you check the authenticity and strength of a hadith before using it to form a belief or action? Reflect on a time you acted on a weak hadith because it suited your desires. What can you do differently now?
?
Are you comfortable with the idea that your actions are included in Allah's eternal knowledge, yet you are still responsible? How does this tension affect your sense of accountability and reliance on Allah's mercy?
